The Executive Yuan Resolved

Appointment of Jian Pai Jin Wen-si to Exchange Treaties with China; Guo Da-ming Appointed New Provincial Government Committee Member; Chang Zhi-zhen Appointed Henan Provincial Government Committee Member; Many Provinces and Cities to Establish Sports Fields 22

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 164th meeting on the morning of the 12th. Those in attendance included Wang Zhaoming, Gu Mengyu, Kong Xiangxi, Shi Qingyang, Wang Shijie, Chen Shuren, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, and others, with Wang Zhaoming presiding.

(A) Reports

(1) Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance reported, requesting that the management of official properties in various counties of Hebei, which should be retained for tenant farmers, be temporarily suspended across the board. All established official property bureaus in the counties should be abolished, and the Office of Official Properties should be temporarily scaled down. Furthermore, the various investigated special cases of official property, as well as cases already handled or not yet handled by the county bureaus, should be promptly submitted to the Ministry for verification and approved for separate handling, in order to conclude these matters. As for how to maintain the livelihoods of banner land leaseholders and how to relieve the living conditions of banner people, it is proposed to devise proper methods separately and then proceed. Please review and record this case.

(B) Review of Reports

(1) Vice Minister Chuan of the Ministry of Interior and the vice chairmen of various ministry and committee commissions reported on the review and determination of methods for performance evaluation. Review opinions: 1. Except for the Ministries of Military Affairs and the Navy, which have specific performance evaluation regulations to follow, all other ministries and commissions should conduct performance evaluations within six days. 2. Regarding rewards and punishments for performance evaluations, in addition to commendations and reprimands, increases in salary and dismissals should be included. Punishments for derelict personnel should also be included. 3. A draft of interim measures for the performance evaluation of the Executive Yuan and its affiliated ministries and commissions is submitted for review and approval. Resolution: Passed.

(C) Appointments and Removals

(1) Resolution: Wu Liande, a member of the Opium Suppression Committee, is to be removed from his post due to other appointments.

(2) Resolution: Hu Sayin Die, a member of the Xinjiang Provincial Government, has requested to resign. His request should be approved, and Guo Daming is appointed as a member of the Xinjiang Provincial Government.

(3) Resolution: Zhang Fang, a member of the Henan Provincial Government, has requested to resign from his post as a member of the provincial government due to his military duties. His request should be approved, and Chang Zhizhen is appointed to succeed him as a member of the Henan Provincial Government.

(4) Minister Wang, concurrently Minister of Foreign Affairs, submitted a request to appoint Jin Wen-si, the Minister Plenipotentiary to the Netherlands, as the Plenipotentiary Representative for the exchange of the Sino-Dutch Friendship Treaty. Resolution: Passed.

(5) Minister Luo of the Judicial Administration Department submitted a request to appoint Mou Zhenxi as the Director of the Zhejiang Rehabilitation Center. Resolution: Passed.

(6) Minister Luo of the Judicial Administration Department submitted a request to have Kong Jiazhang serve as the Presiding Judge of the Tianjin District Court on a trial basis. Resolution: Passed.

(7) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs reported that Shao Fangming, the Director of the Wuchang Leather Factory, has another appointment and requested his removal from his post. It is proposed to fill the vacancy with Liu Xinpan. Resolution: Passed.

(8) Minister Chen of the Navy Department submitted a request to appoint Liu Tianfu as the Naval Attaché with the rank of Colonel at the Embassy in Japan. Resolution: Passed.

(D) Matters for Discussion

(1) The President proposed that a circular be issued to all provincial and municipal governments to establish more sports fields. The scale need not be grand; low cost and practicality should be the main considerations. Rather than building a single large-scale sports field with public funds, it would be better to build narrower sports fields in multiple locations to achieve wider coverage. The detailed measures should be drafted by the Ministry of Education and circulated for implementation. Please make a public decision on this matter. Resolution: Passed. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 12th)

Current Commentary

Recent Changes in the European Situation 23

— Heng

In recent days, the situation in Europe has become tense due to the convening of the Disarmament Conference. It started with the confrontation between Germany and France, followed by disagreements between Britain and France. The frightening nature of the situation is truly reminiscent of the eve of the First World War in 1914. However, not long after, Britain and France shook hands and made peace, reaffirming their cooperation, which allowed the disarmament conference, which was on the verge of collapse, to maintain a glimmer of hope. The deteriorating relationship between France and Germany also showed signs of change. According to recent European dispatches, in addition to Britain and France seeking renewed cooperation, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has also stepped forward to seek a resolution with the German and French authorities. At the same time, the Little Entente's recognition of Soviet Russia has also been established. The speed of changes in the situation has exceeded expectations. However, there are reasons why European countries have pulled back from the brink and are unwilling to quickly create a second world war. The reasons can be summarized in several points.

(1) France has always relied on Britain to assert its influence against Germany. If it loses Britain's sympathy, its power to restrain Germany will be difficult. However, since the Great War, France has been strong and Germany has been weak, so Britain has often suppressed France and helped Germany between the two countries. Even after Hitler came to power, Britain's attitude remained the same. The key to the growing discord between British and French opinions and the growing closeness between French and Russian relations lies in this. If Britain could show a little concession to France, France would rather maintain Britain's goodwill. If Britain can cooperate with France, France's benefits will not only be in Europe, but its position in the Far East can also be maintained. For France, weighing the situation, if it loses Britain and gains Russia, it can certainly restrain Germany in Europe, but its Annam in the Far East will inevitably be threatened by Japan. The French are deeply concerned about this. Therefore, although they have been on the same wavelength with the Russians at the Disarmament Conference, their attitude is also very flexible. As soon as the US representative's mediation arrived, they immediately expressed concessions to Britain, passing a compromise proposal to re-invite Germany. Their intention to not lose Britain by gaining Russia is very clear.

(2) If the union of France and Russia becomes a reality, Britain's situation will be very difficult. Li Weinuofu's proposal includes: one, to conclude a mutual assistance pact; two, to define the definition of aggression; and three, to implement sanctions against aggressor nations. His intention is clearly to bind Britain when Germany invades Russia or attacks France, in order to fight against Germany. If this kind of pact is expanded and implemented in the Far East, then in the event of a Russo-Japanese war, Britain will again bear the responsibility of sanctioning Japan. All of these would make British policy subject to others and lose its opportunity to be flexible and benefit from the situation. Moreover, if France and Russia form a group and fight against the group of Japan and Germany, Britain would not want to help France and Russia fight Germany in Europe, nor would it bother to oppose Japan for Russia in the Far East. Therefore, for Britain's own sake, it is actually not conducive to close cooperation between France and Russia. At this Disarmament Conference, the reason why the British were able to abandon their opinions, turn the tide, and rejoin forces with France was to make France slightly distance itself from its relationship with Russia and not allow Soviet Russia's proposals to be fully realized.

(3) Mussolini is watching intently and observing the changes. He is constantly thinking of using the contradictions between France and Germany and the divisions between Britain and France to expand his group diplomacy since the Austro-Hungarian union. Now, Mr. Mussolini has taken advantage of the disarmament stalemate and stepped forward to invite the responsible authorities from both sides to Italy for consultations. Although this move is nominally mediation, it is difficult to guarantee that there are no other intentions. It may be to recruit Germany and expand the established group, or it may not be known. Furthermore, observing the French Foreign Minister's reluctance to go to Italy, the French are probably already wary of this. If this kind of speculation is not too far off, then today's sudden turn of the Little Entente to recognize Soviet Russia is not without reason. The interests of Austria-Hungary and the Little Entente are inherently contradictory. Since the Austro-Hungarian union, the reason why they have been able to coexist peacefully is because Italy and Germany are suspicious of each other. If the meeting between Mr. Mussolini and Hitler is successful, then the threat to the Little Entente and France will far exceed that of the Austro-German merger. The reason why France today wants to ally with Russia but cannot bear to lose the goodwill of Britain must be related to this.

The situation in Europe is already so complex, and the interests and viewpoints of various countries in the Far East are so different. Under these circumstances, France's relationship with Russia cannot but be kept within limits. If it does not reach the point of despair, it must prioritize maintaining friendship with Britain. However, in order to strengthen international influence, it must still use Soviet Russia to assert its own importance. This is one point. If cooperation between Britain and France can continue, then the League of Nations will certainly still exist. There is still plenty of room for twists and turns in disarmament negotiations. The outbreak of war in Europe can be delayed as a result. This is the second point. As for Germany, if it joins the group of Italy, Austria-Hungary, and it is thought for Germany, there are very few options left for Germany. Germany's demands today are indeed for rearmament. However, the purpose of rearmament must be to seek the recovery of lost territory and the expansion of territory. In this regard, how will the Germans deal with France? In our opinion, the disparity in strength between Germany and France is too great, so they will not easily start a war. As for Poland, they have just signed a ten-year non-aggression treaty, so they will not immediately turn their backs. However, the Baltic countries are small and weak, and it is not difficult to invade them. Lithuania, in particular, is the target of the Germans. Therefore, once Japan and Russia are at war, Germany may take the opportunity to move eastward to launch an invasion of Soviet Russia. It is not impossible. The reason why Soviet Russia is now eagerly conspiring with France to conclude an Eastern European non-aggression pact is to preemptively prevent Germany from taking advantage of others' dangers for its own benefit. With Li Weinuofu's flexible diplomatic skills, Soviet Russia's attempt has a hope of success. Therefore, if the Russo-Japanese war does not break out immediately, Soviet Russia has plenty of time to deal with it calmly. If so, then Germany's way out will still not be able to be opened. This is the third point. Looking at this kind of mutually restrictive relationship, we can see that although the situation in Europe is extremely tense, it is not about to start a war. However, if we think that the European situation has a peaceful atmosphere, it is inevitable that we are too optimistic.

Page 7

Next Year's Naval Disarmament Conference

Britain to Propose Restrictions on Military Aircraft; Expected to be Opposed by the United States; Preliminary Negotiations Between Britain, America, and Japan to Begin Next Week; Italy to Proceed with Shipbuilding Plans; Caused by Japan and France's Competitive Expansion of Their Navies 24

(Tokyo) Preparations for the naval disarmament preliminary conference between Britain, the United States, and Japan are ready. According to Ambassador Matsudaira's report to the Foreign Ministry on the 11th, British Foreign Minister Simon, US Ambassador Bingham, and Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira are scheduled to begin talks next week, regardless of whether they have received responses from France and Italy. It is expected that these talks will proceed smoothly. (Nihon Rengo Tsushin dispatch on the 12th)

(Washington) According to reliable sources today, Britain may request restrictions on naval military aircraft at next year's naval disarmament conference. Britain has not yet specifically stated its position on this important issue. The United States is said to be opposing this. US naval officials insist that the idea of ​​air forces flying across the ocean to bomb enemy cities is an exaggeration, because a large base is needed near the attack location, and battleships must protect it in order to succeed. The naval authorities of Japan and the United States are now preparing new funds to enrich their coastal defense air forces, while Britain is allowing its air force to lag behind and has now fallen to fourth or fifth place. Britain once hoped that the Disarmament Conference would restrict military aircraft. The General Disarmament Committee has now appointed a special committee to study this matter. Impartial observers here believe that civil aircraft can be easily converted for military use, which is the difficulty in managing naval military aircraft. Commercial airfields can also be converted into military airfields. Therefore, the establishment of air force bases in trustee islands and the Aleutian Islands will cause unrest in the Pacific. It is said that several trustee islands have already begun to build commercial airfields, and the base in the Aleutian Islands is being considered. (Guomin News Agency dispatch on the 11th)

The Italian government in Rome has begun construction of two 35,000-ton armored cruisers, estimated to cost 100 million lire and take four years to complete. According to Italy's original shipbuilding plan, in addition to this, there are also six 6,000-ton to 7,000-ton armored cruisers, four destroyers, four small torpedo boats, and twelve submarines. (Havas dispatch on the 11th)

(Rome) An evening newspaper explained the reason why Italy is building two 35,000-ton armored cruisers, saying that Italy originally had the right to build two ships. The reason why they have not yet started construction is to take into account the disarmament conference. Now, not only has the disarmament conference in Geneva not achieved anything, but the Washington Naval Treaty has also gone bankrupt. The results of previous naval conferences have not only failed to eliminate the factors of mutual suspicion and competition between the signatory countries, but the navies of various countries have increased as a result. The naval conference originally took the British Navy as the maximum limit, thinking that it could not be exceeded. Unexpectedly, the Japanese Navy was originally inferior to the British Navy, but it has gradually increased since the naval conference and is now equal to the British Navy. (Havas dispatch on the 11th)

(London) Official circles are paying close attention to Italy's construction of two 35,000-ton armored cruisers. It is generally believed that Italy did not sign the London Naval Treaty, so it has the right to build large tonnage warships. No one has any objection to this matter. However, the general opinion is that if what Italy is doing is the beginning of a new shipbuilding policy, then Britain's plan to prepare for preliminary negotiations at the 1935 naval conference may be greatly revised as a result, and Britain's policy before and during the naval conference will be considerably affected by Italy's new policy. The country directly affected by Italy's shipbuilding plan is France, because the reason why the French government failed to recognize the 1930 London Naval Treaty was that Italy demanded equality with the French Navy. This time, Italy's shipbuilding plan is a re-raising of the naval equality issue. (Havas dispatch on the 11th)

Disarmament Conference Adjourned Indefinitely; Four Committees Formed to Continue Work; Britain, Italy, and Hungary Disagree with the Security Pact; Disarmament Chairman Hopes Germany Will Return to the Conference 25

After the General Committee of the Reuters Disarmament Conference met today, it elected representatives of European countries to form a Security Committee to consider the issue of regional security pacts in accordance with the tripartite compromise resolution passed last Friday. However, Hungary and Italy both stated that they reserved their positions and were only observers. The chairman of today's General Committee meeting was the Greek politician Politis, who was elected on the proposal of Henderson. The only diplomatic officials who attended the meeting were the Soviet Union's Li Weinuofu, who did not arrive until half an hour after the meeting began. Mr. Li said that he hoped that the security pact would include countries outside Europe in the future, not only regionally but universally. Mrs. Axu Pei, a well-known social affairs expert, who has represented Britain at the Disarmament Conference for more than two years, read an article stating that Britain could not participate in any pact other than the Locarno Pact. Henderson then stated that he would send the Soviet Union's proposal to change the Disarmament Conference into a permanent organization called the "Peace Conference" to the governments concerned, and also said that if the negotiations between the governments regarding Germany's return to the conference could not achieve the desired progress, he intended to convene the main leaders to discuss the matter. The General Committee then announced an indefinite adjournment at 5:20 p.m., after deliberating for one hour and thirty-five minutes.

(Reuters dispatch on the 12th)

(Geneva) The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference met, chaired by Henderson. The various committees were immediately organized according to the compromise proposal made by Bartou to carry out their work. (1) The Security Committee, composed of representatives of European countries, was chaired by the Greek representative, Politis. Countries outside Europe were welcome to participate. (2) The Second Committee discussed issues related to monitoring and guaranteeing the implementation of the disarmament treaty, chaired by the Belgian representative, Poolgan. (3) The Third Committee studied aviation issues, chaired by the Spanish representative, Madariaga. (4) The Fourth Committee studied the manufacture and sale of weapons, chaired by the Danish representative, Skavenius. As for the Soviet Union's proposal to change the Disarmament Conference into a "Permanent Conference for Guaranteeing Peace," it was immediately sent to various governments for their opinions. The organization of the Security Committee aroused reservations from various parties. The first was Hungarian representative General Donaz, who said that a security pact could not be established without leaving the nature of the world, and said that he would participate in the work of the Security Committee as an observer. The second was Italian representative Sulania, who said that when the resolution proposed by France was passed by the General Committee by a majority, the Italian delegation was not among those who approved it. Therefore, the Italian representative would also participate in the Security Committee as an observer. The third was British representative Asbi, who said that although Britain sent personnel to participate in the Security Committee, it believed that Britain did not necessarily have to participate in any new regional security pacts established in Europe in the future. French representative Massigli declared that the French delegation acknowledged its participation in the Security Committee and said, "Cooperation in good faith from all parties is not without benefit. The attitude adopted by the Italian delegation stems from the country's principles regarding the entire work of the Disarmament Conference. As for the Hungarian representative, he deeply hoped that he would understand the benefits of the Security Committee and actively participate in it. Soviet representative Li Weinuofu said that the European Security Pact does not exclude other pacts, just as regional treaties can still be separately signed by various countries in addition to a globally concluded pact. The suggestion made by Chairman Henderson was thus passed. It was decided that the draft convention drafted by the special committee, which contained a form for various military expenditures, should be reported by the governments of various countries to the Disarmament Conference in accordance with the form. The Presidium would reconvene after the actions of the various governments were clear. However, if the various countries procrastinate, the Presidium should still convene. When the meeting was adjourned, Henderson said that he warmly hoped that the various governments would take action so that the disarmament issue could be resolved, and Germany could return to Geneva. (Havas dispatch on the 11th)

(Geneva) The committee of the Disarmament Conference that studies the issue of monitoring armaments and guaranteeing the implementation of the disarmament treaty, chaired by the Belgian representative Poolgan, is scheduled to begin its meetings starting this Wednesday. The committee dealing with security issues will meet in the middle of next week. It is generally believed that the Aviation Issues Committee will be able to meet at the beginning of July, after French Foreign Minister Bartou goes to Britain. (Havas dispatch on the 11th)

(London) The Times today published an editorial expressing satisfaction with the efforts to maintain the Disarmament Conference, saying that if the Disarmament Conference were to dissolve, it would be difficult to reopen negotiations. The newspaper further stated that the resolution passed in Geneva on Friday mentioned the British, German, French, and Italian communiques, in which three countries recognized Germany's right to restore considerable armaments. Therefore, the French government must deeply consider Germany's proposal to restore armaments. If Germany's right to establish self-defense armaments is not recognized, then disarmament has no hope of concluding a convention. If that is the case, then an arms race is its only way out, which is beneficial to countries with substantial national power, but not beneficial to countries with budgets that are not. (Guomin News Agency dispatch on the 11th)

Embargo on Bolivian and Paraguayan Armaments, Italy and Germany Add Conditions, Participation Only if Other Countries Comply Similarly, Ban Likely Unachievable 33

(London) Italy's attitude towards the ban on arms shipments to Paraguay and Bolivia is causing anxiety to those in Britain who are associated with the League of Nations. Italy has put forward two conditions: (1) that both Japan and Russia agree to the embargo, and (2) that all arms ordered by Bolivia and Paraguay from Italy, both for immediate and future delivery, should not be subject to the ban. If these two conditions can be met, Italy will agree to accept the embargo. Regarding the first condition, although Russia has joined, Japan seems to have refused. Association with the League of Nations and, in practice, the participation of Japan and Russia is an indispensable condition for the arms embargo, because neither country has ever shipped arms to Bolivia and Paraguay. As for the second condition, the stipulation regarding future deliveries is sufficient to make the embargo impossible to implement. Italy's raising of this condition is tantamount to refusing to participate in the embargo. People here generally hope that, since all countries have unanimously agreed, Italy will change its mind and no longer insist on its conditions. (Havas, 11th)

(Geneva) The British Ambassador to Germany cabled that the German government declared that Germany is willing to abide by the League of Nations declaration of March 1933, prohibiting the shipment of war materials to Paraguay and Bolivia, provided that other countries also comply in the same way. This cable has been communicated today by the British legal affairs representative to the League of Nations to the three-member committee handling the arms embargo. (Reuters, 11th)

US Congress Passes Silver Bill, Three Important Amendments Rejected, Mineral and Industrial Uses Exempt from Profit Tax 37

(Washington) The Senate passed the Silver Bill this morning by a vote of fifty-four to twenty-five. Three amendments were rejected, but a minor amendment was passed, stipulating that silver mines or industrial uses of silver are exempt from the 50% profit tax, while the original proposal for collecting a speculative profit tax on silver remains. An amendment proposed by senators to set the gold-silver ratio at sixteen or seventeen to one, and to freely coin silver, was rejected by a vote of fifty-nine to eighteen. Government-affiliated senators also rejected Thomas' amendment, which argued for setting the standard for currency reserves at 75% gold and 25% silver based on the market price of silver rather than its monetary value, by a vote of sixty-five to seventeen. After passing the Silver Bill, the Senate sent it to a joint committee to resolve differences with the House regarding the profit tax. There was a brief debate before the bill was passed. Senator Borah called for a thorough reform of the national monetary system to prevent wealth from being concentrated in the hands of a few. Borah considered the gold standard and the World War to be the causes of today's global depression and strongly supported the Silver Bill, recognizing the current Silver Bill as a legitimate step, but not recognizing that it has solved the fundamental problems of the monetary system. Borah further advocated immediately minting silver coins with the aim of world trade. Senator King also delivered a speech defending the Silver Bill, saying that President Roosevelt will conclude silver agreements with various countries to raise and stabilize prices and believing that this plan will definitely benefit the world. Senator Hatfield opposed the Silver Bill, calling it a superfluous burden and saying that there is no need to expand currency reserves, with gold reserves exceeding the existing currency reserve by five times. The Silver Bill passed by both houses of Congress stipulates that increasing the gold-silver reserve ratio is the policy of the United States, its ultimate goal being to create and maintain a silver base of one-fourth of the total reserves. It also stipulates that the Secretary of the Treasury is authorized and directed to purchase silver at home and abroad with US legal tender or funds not otherwise appropriated, and that the Secretary of the Treasury has the authority to handle delivery and prices, etc., as he deems beneficial to the United States. However, the bill also restricts the power of the Secretary of the Treasury, stipulating that the Secretary of the Treasury has no right to purchase silver under the following circumstances: (1) when the market price of silver is higher than the monetary value of silver; (2) when silver stocks are equal to or exceed 25% of the total gold and silver stocks; (3) when the price of silver exceeds 50 cents per ounce. The Silver Bill stipulates that silver shall be nationalized, allowing this provision to be permissive rather than mandatory. The provision stipulates that when the President deems it necessary to control the price of US currency, he may issue an order to hand over privately owned silver to the mint to mint silver coins or as a currency fund. (National Telegram, 11th)

(Washington) Following the House of Representatives, the Senate today passed the Silver Bill. This bill was proposed by silver advocates who wanted to establish measures to support silver during this congressional session. This bill stipulates increasing US silver reserves, allowing the President to accept domestic monetary silver reserves, and allowing the Secretary of the Treasury to purchase silver on domestic and foreign markets at prices, times, and methods that he deems most beneficial to the public interest. For domestic purchases, the price of silver held as of May 1 is limited to 50 cents per ounce. It also allows the Secretary of the Treasury to sell silver when the price of silver exceeds its monetary value, or when monetary silver exceeds the gold-silver ratio of four to one, and allows the Secretary of the Treasury to issue silver certificates, the face value of which shall not be lower than the cost of the silver purchased. This bill also authorizes the Secretary of the Treasury to manage investigations and prohibits the purchase, import, and transfer of silver, violators of which may be subject to a fine of $10,000 or imprisonment for up to ten years. The Secretary of the Treasury may also issue regulations that he deems necessary to implement this bill. (Reuters, 11th)

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that the New York Federal Assay Office has now received 5 million ounces of silver shipped from London. Well-informed sources here believe that this silver was purchased several weeks ago for use in the equalization fund. This matter has aroused great interest here, because after the Senate passed the Silver Bill this afternoon, it is unknown to what extent the President and the Treasury Department will use the powers conferred by the bill. (National Telegram, 11th)

France, Belgium, Czech Republic Refuse to Pay US War Debts 38

(Washington) Belgium and the Czech Republic have notified the United States that they will refuse to pay war debts, and the French Cabinet has also formally decided to notify the US government that it will suspend payment of debt installments due on Friday. This matter was long expected and therefore did not attract any attention. France must pay the United States a total of $6,847,674,104.10 in principal and interest, but so far only $486,075,891 has been repaid. According to the US State Department's prediction, other debtor countries will follow suit and declare their refusal to pay war debts. Belgium owes the United States a total of $727,830,000 in war debts. The debt due on June 15 is $1,125,000. Belgium has repaid a total of $52,191,273 to the United States, but the last two installments have not yet been paid. The Czech Republic should repay the United States $312,811,432, of which only $19,804,178 has been paid to date. (National Telegram, 11th)

Ministry of Finance Stipulates Standards for Handling Local Budgets 52

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has stipulated five standards for handling local budgets and has notified the provincial and municipal governments to comply with them: (1) Reorganizing local finances should primarily focus on living within one's means. (2) Local governments should handle administrative affairs, carefully consider their urgency, and strive to save wasteful expenses to ensure that income and expenditure are balanced. (3) The budget for the 23rd year urgently needs to be prepared. Local governments should uphold the central government's intentions, make real cuts in expenditures within the scope of not harming necessary affairs, and compile a preliminary estimate to be submitted for approval. (4) If the preliminary estimates compiled by the counties are inflated or inappropriate, they should be strictly rejected. (5) After the budget is determined, if the counties have surplus funds, they should be remitted to the provincial treasury. If the provincial treasury has surplus funds, it should be reported to the central government for approval to be stored for the province's local construction. The county budget will be approved by the province, and if there is a shortfall, the provincial treasury will find ways to subsidize it. The provincial budget will be approved by the central government, and if there is a shortfall, the central government will find ways to subsidize it. (Special Telegram, 12th)

After the Health Office conducted chemical tests using scientific methods, no toxins were found. International Commercial Telegrams: Special Reuters Business Report for June 12th 74

Gold and Silver: London Gold Prices: The London gold price today is 137 shillings and 7.5 pence, down 2 pence.

London Silver Bar: London silver spot price is 19 pence 625, futures price is 19 pence 6875, both down 0.0625. India bought and China sold in the morning, with light trading.

New York Silver Bar: The silver market in New York is sluggish, and merchants are disappointed. The general opinion is that the silver bill will hinder legitimate transactions and speculative activities. There are rumors from several sources that there may be test cases regarding the tax payment.

Bombay Silver Bar: The Bombay silver market is stable today. The spot price is down 4 annas to 54 rupees 14 annas, and futures are down 4 pounds each.

Exchange Rates 75

The opening exchange rate for British pounds to US dollars was 5.06125, the same as yesterday's closing rate for US dollars to British pounds. Germany Actively Engaged in Military Construction (Berlin Dispatch): Budget Expansion, Booming Military Industry, Deteriorating Relations with the Soviet Union, Increased Vigilance Against France 80

The European political situation, with no results from the Disarmament Conference and the League of Nations lacking vitality, shows an increasingly obvious antagonism between Germany and France, leading to an increasingly tense situation. The German people are quite convinced that Germans cannot stand naked against armed enemies, so they withdrew from the Disarmament Conference and the League of Nations to show their determination. As for the domestic situation in Germany, when Hitler first came to power in January last year, the number of unemployed workers accounted for almost one-third of all workers, with a real number of over six million. By the end of last year, there were only four million. In January and February of this year, the numbers should have increased due to seasonal factors, but in fact, January had 3.774 million, February had 3.374 million, March decreased to 2.8 million, and at the end of April it decreased by another 191,000 to 2.609 million. Compared to last year, there is a clear improvement.

However, these figures only include those with unemployment insurance or receiving other relief. In addition, there are at least 1.5 million unregistered unemployed people. When asked about the reasons for the improvement, officials say it is due to reducing working hours, emergency civil engineering projects, and abolishing female workers, leading them back to the kitchen, etc. While these measures have had some effect, in reality, the main reason should be the expansion of the military budget and the booming of the military industry.

(1) The budget under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of National Defense for the fiscal year 1934 totals 890 million marks, of which the army accounts for 654 million marks, the navy accounts for 236 million marks, and the air force has an additional 210 million marks. The subsidies for the Stormtroopers and voluntary labor amount to 250 million marks. All of these can be regarded as national defense expenditures, totaling 1.35 billion marks.

(2) The Ministry of National Defense is responsible for guiding the industrial mobilization of all of Germany, building new factories, and repairing old machinery. Wartime industrial activities have already resumed. This is evidenced by the fact that all military industrial stocks on the Berlin Stock Market rose sharply at the end of last year. Furthermore, in German foreign trade statistics, the import of raw materials for the military industry has increased dramatically, while the export of manufactured goods has suddenly decreased. Industries such as Rheinmetall Krupp, Moersel Berlin, Galsel leaves, etc., as well as military supply factories such as Zeiss, Siemens, etc., the poison gas factory of the Egger dye factory, and engine manufacturers such as Bayern, have all greatly increased their number of workers.

In this situation, after the exhaustion of Germany after the war, restricted by the Treaty of Versailles and burdened by financial and economic difficulties, it is difficult to form a strong army. However, she still does not flinch, striving forward for progress.

The German army is allowed only 100,000 men under the Treaty of Versailles, but these 100,000 men are all excellent cadre officers, and the number of people voluntarily enlisting is about ten times the quota, so the value of the army is very high. Although this military organization is new, it is completely inherited from the tradition of the old army. Its unity is centered on President Hindenburg. Although not many swear loyalty to the old German Emperor, the feudal atmosphere is very strong. Anyone with connections to the Communist Party is very difficult to be selected.

Germany has always had deep hostility towards France and Poland, so it was very close to the Soviet Union. Recently, German-Soviet relations have deteriorated, but she is still greatly influenced by the Red Army. For example, in the organization of equipment, in tactical thinking, and in education and training, these factors still remain. The Military Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of National Defense is similar in nature to the General Staff Headquarters before the war, and its powers are also similar, and it uses this to train the officers it needs.

The number of the army has not changed much in terms of organization, but the equipment has been strengthened. The number of personnel has also increased from 100,000 to 165,000. There are also 100,000 trained reservists and 150,000 police who can be used as auxiliary troops. The SA SS Stormtroopers belonging to the Nazi Party are entirely military organizations, and some are even armed. The number of people who have been trained is over one million. The navy has her pocket battleship, and the air force is also preparing five bomber squadrons and ten to twelve fighter squadrons. In short, Germany is actively engaged in military construction. France, witnessing its military expansion, will naturally accelerate the completion of its air force expansion plan to guard against German retaliation. Therefore, the situation between the two countries has become tense again. (May 1st, Berlin)

The Kang-Tibetan Dispute: Great Disparity in Border Demarcation Opinions; Huang Emissary Attempts Reconciliation from a Religious Perspective 81

Ya'an Dispatch: Huang Musong, the special envoy dispatched by the central government to Tibet to pay respects to the Dalai Lama, arrived in Kangding from Ya'an together with Tang Ying, the commander of the Xikang Reclamation, Yu Ruhai, the special envoy for Kang-Tibetan peace, and others. The Sichuan-Xikang Border Defense Headquarters received a telegram from Kangding stating that Huang, Tang, and others had safely arrived in Kangding. Various agencies in Kangding and Han and Yi people held grand welcome ceremonies. As for Huang's mission to Tibet this time, it is because the Kang-Tibetan dispute has not been resolved for a long time. The central government is paying attention to the western border defense, so it specifically ordered Huang to take the route through Sichuan and Kang to investigate the truth of the Kang-Tibetan dispute in order to resolve it as the opportunity arises. Therefore, Liu Wenhui, the commander of the Sichuan-Xikang Border Defense Headquarters, specifically convened Xiang Yuren, Tang Ying, Yu Ruhai, Liu Yuanzhang, and others when Huang arrived in Ya'an to discuss specific methods for resolving the Kang-Tibetan dispute, to offer to Huang, and specifically appointed Yu Ruhai as the special envoy for Kang-Tibetan peace, intending for Huang to mediate between them so that both sides would return to good terms and end the dispute forever. It is heard that Liu's opinion on resolving the Kang-Tibetan dispute is to take the clear demarcation of the Kang-Tibetan border as a prerequisite. However, the question of where the Kang-Tibetan border should be is quite complex, with much controversy and no agreement. Liu Wenhui's opinion is that the Kang-Tibetan border must be drawn to Chamdo at a minimum. If this issue can be resolved appropriately, other issues such as the restoration of the Da Jin Temple and the placement of the Da Jin surname can be easily resolved. It is heard that Huang also quite agrees with his statement. However, the ideal border in the Tibetan imagination is vastly different from this. The Qionglai Mountains and the Luding Iron Bridge, which were proposed in the past, need not be mentioned. Even the Taining Temple, which was proposed in recent years, and the "Han army must withdraw to Rongba Cha" proposed by Qiong Rang's representative Xiang Jiang Yuwen at the Ada Conference a month ago, differ so greatly that they cannot be measured by distance. It is feared that even with Huang's mediation, it will be difficult to resolve.

According to the Kangbei front-line report on the recent situation of the Tibetan side received by the Sichuan-Xikang Military Headquarters, Tibet is currently divided into three major factions: one is the county government faction, to which Reting Hutuktu and the Kashag belong, with the Dalai Lama's followers as its backbone, advocating the continued maintenance of the current regime; one is the old faction, also known as the pro-China faction, advocating welcoming the Panchen Lama back to Tibet to preside over political power; one is the youth faction, most of whom are students who have studied in England, so they have the name of the pro-British faction, advocating the creation of an independent status for Tibet. The representatives of the Tibetan army stationed on the Kang border mostly belong to this faction.

When Huang Musong set off from Ya'an to Kang a few days ago, he telegraphed the current authorities in Tibet, stating that to solve the Tibetan problem, one must start from religion and then promote politics from religion. Except for national defense, diplomacy, and major international negotiations, which are directly handled by the central government, all other matters are handled by the Tibetan government itself. As for the development of Tibet and education and transportation in Tibet, the central government will provide financial and human assistance and welcome Tibetan youth to study in the mainland to bridge the feelings between the Han and Tibetan nationalities. As for the subsidies that the three major monasteries in Lhasa received during the Qing Dynasty, they will all be restored uniformly and allocated by the central government. It is heard that the Tibetan government is extremely gratified by Huang's entry into Kang and has sent senior officials to Chamdo to greet him.

On the West Bank of the Gan River, Bandits Are Defeated One After Another; Gao Yongsheng Is Captured Alive; Xu Yangang's Troops Are Scattered; Many of Xiao Ke's Bandits Are Killed 82

Nanchang Dispatch: The bandits to the west of the Gan River, as far as southern Hubei and eastern Hunan, are divided into two puppet military regions: (1) the puppet Gan-E-Xiang Military Region, whose puppet commander was originally Kong Hechong, who also served as the commander-in-chief of the puppet Sixth Army Corps, under whose jurisdiction were the bandit troops of the puppet Sixteenth Division Gao Yongsheng and the Independent 123rd Division Ye Jinbo, etc., based in the contiguous mountainous areas of Xiutong in western Jiangxi north of Pingxiang, Pingliu in eastern Hunan, and Chongtong Yangxin in southern Hubei, and with its vicinity as a guerrilla zone, the Nanxun and E-Xiang railways being their only target for sabotage; (2) the puppet Gan-Xiang Military Region, whose commander was originally Li Tianzhu, who also served as the commander of the puppet Eighth Army. Li's bandits have recently disappeared and are being presided over by Xiao Ke. Under his jurisdiction are the puppet Seventeenth and Eighteenth Divisions and the puppet Gan-Xiang Independent Division, using the dangerous mountainous area of Huaxi, contiguous to Yongxin, Anfu, Lianhua, and Suichuan, as a nest, appearing and disappearing in Sui, Wan, Tai, Anji, Lianning, Yong, and Cha-You, and constantly trying to cross the Gan River to respond to the bandits on the east bank of the Gan River. The above two groups are solely tasked with disrupting the rear and containing the national army's suppression efforts. Although no counties within the defense area of the Western Route Army's jurisdiction, which includes forty-three counties, have been captured by bandits, scattered bandits in the four countryside areas of the above counties are still constantly roaming and harassing. The 123rd Detachment and other detachments are also constantly pursuing and intercepting them.

Gao Yongsheng had previously invaded Gao'an Dongxin and Nanxun Road Ma Jiongling to loot, and then led the remnants to escape into the mountains of Xiushui. According to political news, Commissioner Cao of the Third Administrative District Commissioner's Office received a telephone call from Xiushui County stating that the ninth squadron of the county had advanced to Zhongfeng on the ninth and captured a puppet Sixteenth Division Commander Gao Yongsheng. After receiving the telephone call, Commissioner Cao immediately sent Deputy Regiment Commander Wu with a company of soldiers to Xiushui to escort the bandit to the province for investigation.

Xu Yangang, the puppet commander who recently raided Anyi County, withdrew from the county on the 2nd and fled north. On the 4th, he was intercepted by Yue Sen's division at Tan Shen Temple and split into two. Important documents, telephones, mimeographs, etc. of the puppet command of Xu's bandits were captured by the division. Xu himself escaped and fled into the mountains of Tailangling. He is currently being searched for. Yue Sen has telegraphed the province to report, stating, "Xu's bandits fled north. It is judged that they must pass through Tanxi. When Li's regiment of this division took a shortcut from Jiaoyuan overnight to Tan Shen Hall, they happened to encounter the bandits crossing here and were attacked by our vanguard troops, cutting the bandits into two sections. According to captured bandits, 'Only the vanguard battalion passed through, and Xu was behind.' A part will encircle north, and a large part will encircle south. After about two hours of battle, all the bandits were defeated, and countless were injured and killed. The remnants fled in a disorderly manner to Taiziling and Snake Pit Ridge. They are currently being searched for in separate ways. This battle was a surprise attack on the puppet command, capturing various plans, charts, official document boxes, telephones, and 92 rifles, 2 pistols, 5 mules and horses, and capturing more than 20 bandit officers and soldiers, rescuing more than 40 hostages. All the belongings and luggage of the puppet unit were abandoned and exhausted, and they were very embarrassed."

Xiao Ke's puppet Seventeenth and Eighteenth Divisions on the west bank of the Gan River repeatedly attacked Wan'an Taihe unsuccessfully and retreated into the dangerous mountainous area of Macen Donghua Mountain. On the 3rd, the Western Route Army Peng Weiren's division advanced to suppress them and defeated the puppet Seventeenth and Eighteenth Divisions, killing thousands of bandits. They are still advancing towards Macen. Liu Jianxu has telegraphed Jiang to report victory, stating, "Commander Peng's troops advanced towards the bandits in the Chazishan, Macen, and Donghua Mountain areas on Jiang Day. At dawn on Jiang Day, our vanguard attacked along Chazishan. The bandits resisted stubbornly. Our army attacked fiercely and defeated the bandits. Jiang Chen occupied the bandits' strong positions on several lines of Chazishan Macen. When attacking the highlands near Macen East, Xiao's bandits led the puppet Seventeenth and Eighteenth Divisions to launch a fierce counterattack. The battle was extremely fierce. Thanks to our officers and soldiers, who were extremely brave, and after three hours of fierce fighting, they finally defeated the bandits. In this battle, nearly a thousand bandit officers and soldiers were wounded and killed, and many were captured. Our army suffered minor casualties." (June 10)

Guangzhou Ferry Steamer Boiler Explosion Tragedy: Thirty-three Bodies Recovered; Ship Loss of Over Ten Thousand Yuan 83

Guangzhou Dispatch: Xinzhao Township, Panyu County, Guangdong Province, is the seat of the county government, located near Huangpu. The Pearl River runs through it, making waterway transportation convenient. The Panyu County Government moved to the area two years ago, making Xinzhao Market the key political and commercial area of the county. Traffic to and from Guangzhou is frequent, so there are as many as four ferries operating between Xinzhao and Guangzhou, making over ten trips a day. Among them, the Yi Shun ferry is owned by Liang Guangji Shipping Company. The volume of the ferry is larger than other ships, and it carries more cargo and passengers. As usual, it departs from the old Haizhu Park front dock on Changdi, Guangzhou, at 8:00 AM every day to Xinzhao Market. The ferry hires the Yu Li small steamer to tow it. All has been peaceful. On the morning of the 6th of this month, the ferry was carrying about 200 passengers returning home from the province. It departed at 8:30 AM. As a rule, when ferries are in the provincial river, small steamers must not use cables to tow the ferry. They must be close to each other. Those heading east must be inspected by the Dongguan Customs before using long cables to separate the steamers and ferries to be towed one after the other. When the Yi Shun and Yu Li steamers were opened together, just as they reached the Nan Di river surface, the water boiler of the Yu Li steamer suddenly exploded due to excessive steam pressure, causing a terrible tragedy to occur suddenly. The explosive force was even greater than a 50-pound bomb. At that time, the Yu Li steamer had been blown into pieces and went with the turbulent flow. Eight or nine people on board, including shipmates Liang Bingyao, Tan Jinwu, and shipowner Liu Chengtang, were all dismembered by the blasted iron branches and none survived. At the same time, the Yi Shun ferry, which was close to the left, was also blown into two pieces. More than a hundred passengers on board fell to the east and west. Some were killed on the spot, some escaped into the water, and some drowned due to injuries. The cries shook the sky and it was too terrible to hear. Fortunately, the ship had not yet left the urban area and the accident occurred on the Nan Di river surface, so in an instant, the Jinghua fire ship, the Civil Ship Association, the water police lifeboat, and the Sea Scout lifeboat all rushed to rescue one after another. The Fangbian Hospital on land, the Fire Brigade Headquarters, the Charitable Fire Brigade, the Police Hospital, the Zhongda Hospital, the Guanghua Hospital, and the Qianghua Ambulance Team also gathered at Nan Di for support. When the Jinghua fire ship approached the disaster ship, it first rescued more than 20 injured passengers waiting for rescue. Later, because the disaster ship was blocking the center of the river, it was inconvenient to rescue, so the sunken Yi Shun ferry was towed to the ordnance factory dock on Nan Di to facilitate work. First, hospital ambulances took the rescued injured to the Zhongda Hospital, Guanghua Hospital, and Fangbian Hospital for treatment. The fire brigade continued to salvage corpses, opening up the sunken cabin, counting more than 20 male and female corpses, transporting them to the Fangbian Hospital, taking photos and numbering them, waiting for relatives to identify them. Four more were fished out on the 7th. The ship carried about 100 passengers and about 200 shipmates. In addition to rescuing more than 60 injured people, a total of 33 corpses were recovered. The rest are said to have drowned and buried in the bellies of fish. As of the next day (the 7th), the remains of 15 of the victims had been identified and claimed by their families, and 18 more were awaiting identification and claiming. It is said that there were two cases in which entire families died, which is also tragic. As for the unclaimed corpses, the corpses had rotted and were temporarily buried by the Fangbian Hospital in the Yiba Sha Yidi in the suburbs for the purpose of later relatives’ claiming. As for the injured, there were more than ten people being treated in Zhongda, Guanghua, and Fangbian hospitals, and eleven severely injured were sent to the Municipal Hospital for treatment. Among them, one named Zhong Jingqing died of his injuries that night. The rest of the slightly injured have been discharged from the hospital one after another. The Fangbian Hospital and various fire brigades have continued to salvage corpses for several days, and it is thought that there may be more salvage. This tragedy not only took the lives of innocent refugees, but also caused the shipping company to lose over 100,000 yuan due to the destruction and sinking of the steamer and ferry. (7th)

Canal Dredging Plan: Establishment of a Canal Management Committee with a Budget of 9 Million Yuan 84

Zhenjiang News: China's entire canal system, from Beitongzhou in Hebei Province in the north, passing through Nantongzhou in Jiangsu Province in the east, across the river to Hangzhou in Zhejiang Province, is divided into four sections: the North Canal, the Central Canal, the Inner Canal, and the South Canal. Recently, due to years of neglect, the entire canal system has become severely silted up. In years of heavy rainfall, it causes widespread flooding, damaging farmland along both banks. Furthermore, shipping traffic is frequently blocked. Currently, nine organizations, including the Huai River Conservancy Commission, the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission, the North China Water Conservancy Commission, the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission, and the Construction Departments of Jiangsu, Shandong, Zhejiang, and Hebei provinces, have formed a Canal Management Committee to dredge the entire canal system. The work will be carried out in two phases.

For the surveying work, a surveying team will be formed to conduct preliminary surveys. Mr. Wang Huzhen and Mr. Li Ganfu have been specially appointed as the Chief Engineers of the committee. Mr. Wang previously served as the Chief Engineer of the Huai River Conservancy and the Director of the Anhui-Huai River Engineering Bureau. Surveying has already commenced, starting from Beitongzhou in Hebei Province and extending to the Shandong border. It is expected to be completed by the end of this month. Chief Engineer Wang has been dispatched for several days to survey the Central Canal in Jiangsu Province, and is expected to arrive at Qingjiangpu around mid-July to commence surveying southward along the canal.

Regarding the construction of embankments and dredging of the river, the existing embankments along the north and south banks of the canal are in disrepair and prone to collapse. During heavy rains, there is a risk of breaches and overflows. Therefore, embankment construction is essential for dredging. It is proposed to adopt a similar method as the Six-Tang River dredging project, where the governments of Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang provinces will instruct the county governments along the canal to be responsible for requisitioning labor for dredging. Each county will establish a work section office, and each province will establish an engineering sub-office. The general engineering office for the entire canal dredging project will be located in Nanjing. The total project cost is estimated at 9 million yuan, to be borne by the governments of Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang provinces, as well as the National Economic Council. The four provincial governments will contribute half of the amount, and the remaining half will be borne by the National Economic Council. Construction will officially commence upon the collection of funds. (12th)

Recent Implementation of Land Administration Work in Jiangsu Province 85

Promulgation of Provisional Simplified Rules for Sub-Household Surveying

Zhenjiang News: The Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau has recently been making every effort to advance various land administration tasks. The implementation status of its main tasks is summarized as follows:

Page 10

(1) Land Registration Consolidation: The main task of land registration consolidation is land survey. Jiangsu Province has been preparing for land consolidation since 1927, and it has been over six years. However, no county has fully completed household land surveys (only two districts each in Zhenjiang and Qingpu, and one district in Danyang have been completed, and no entire district has been completed in other counties). The slowness of the original land survey work can be imagined, and the urgent need to improve the original land survey methods is self-evident. In March of this year, the Provincial Government received a telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requiring the completion of the preliminary work of the land survey by the end of March 1935. The Provincial Land Bureau immediately complied with the order and made some improvements to the original land survey methods, which were deliberated, approved, and promulgated by the Provincial Government meeting, and reported to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Subsequently, the bureau formulated implementation measures based on the plan and ordered the land survey teams in various counties to start implementing them from May 1. In the past month, the staff of each team has been working diligently, and the work is progressing smoothly. If the work is carried out at the current rate, in accordance with the prescribed steps, and in an orderly manner, the preliminary work of the land survey in the province can be completed within one year, and the entire land consolidation work can be completed within three years. Once completed as soon as possible, all land disputes can be eliminated accordingly. Recently, local figures from Fengxian and other counties had some misunderstandings about the clauses of the land survey plan promulgated by the Provincial Government, which led to suspicions and requests to the bureau to maintain the original land survey methods. The bureau responded with explanations and dispatched personnel to the counties to convene the submitters together with the county magistrate to explain in detail, and they have been able to fully understand. The local people's deep concern for land survey work shows that land consolidation is urgently needed. It is heard that the bureau believes that land survey work is originally a local undertaking and should be assisted by local people. Therefore, the opinions contributed by local people will be adopted as much as possible within the scope that does not hinder the work, in order to maximize the benefits of implementation. If the land consolidation work in the counties can be assisted by local people at any time in the future, the progress of the work will be smoother. The Provisional Simplified Rules for Sub-Household Surveying promulgated by the bureau are recorded as follows: Article 1: These rules are formulated in accordance with the Jiangsu Provincial Land Survey Standard for Various Business Work and the item of the achievements that each person should have every day. Article 2: The purpose of sub-household surveying is to determine the shape and area of each piece of land (a 1/10,000 land shape map is made from the results of sub-household surveying). Article 3: Sub-household surveying uses a tacheometer, and is carried out using methods such as the optical method, the semi-conductor method, and the intersection method. Article 4: The scale of sub-household surveying shall be in accordance with the following provisions: 1. Ordinary farmland shall use a scale of 1/2000. 2. Urban land or areas with particularly high land prices shall use a scale of 1/1000 or 1/500. 3. Mountainous areas, tidal flats, wasteland, and other areas with low land prices may use a scale of 1/4000 to 1/10,000 as appropriate. Article 5: The map frame of the original map for sub-household surveying shall be rectangular, 40 cm "long" from north to south and 50 cm "wide" from east to west. When a piece of land is cut off by the map frame line, its entire part shall be surveyed and drawn outside the map frame line of the original map that can contain most of it. If a piece of land is too large to be surveyed and drawn in its entirety on any original map, it may be cut off according to the map frame line. Article 6: Sub-household surveying shall be carried out by township (or district). After a township (or district) is surveyed, map assembly, inking, and land number coding procedures shall be carried out in accordance with the map making rules, and a transparent paper shall be used to copy and transcribe the map. Article 7: The production of the original map and the transcribed map shall be detailed separately in the Provisional Rules for Map Making. Article 8: Land number coding shall be carried out by township (or district), and each township (or district) shall be the starting and ending point. It shall be coded with Arabic numerals in a reverse arc, positive arc, or upward arc coding method. The reverse arc, positive arc, and upward arc coding styles are attached below. Article 9: During sub-household surveying, the land use of the first piece of land shall be checked on site and filled in the center of each piece's shape. Article 10: The land uses are defined as follows: 1. Residential land, including residential houses, shops, factories, ancestral halls, temples, churches, schools, government offices, military camps, and undeveloped land in urban areas, as well as ponds, drying grounds, and gardens attached to residential land. 2. Agricultural land, including paddy fields, dry fields, orchards, mulberry fields, medicinal herb land, farms, nurseries, and bamboo land less than 10 mu. 3. Forest land, including bamboo forests and forests of 10 mu or more. 4. Mining land, including mines, mineral springs, salt fields, salt lands, etc. 5. Miscellaneous land, including fish ponds, water chestnut ponds, lotus ponds, water ponds, firewood hills, grass hills, stone hills, reed fields, grasslands, beaches, sandbars, shellfish farms, pastures, docks, loading and unloading yards, private dikes, private ditches, parks, playgrounds, pastures, forts, etc. Roads, rivers, embankments, city walls, railways, etc., shall be coded separately. Article 11: For the sake of accuracy and speed in sub-household surveying, the owners should be notified to participate in the work at any time. Article 12: Roads wider than one meter shall be surveyed. Article 13: Lakes, rivers, ditches, etc., shall be surveyed according to their shapes. Article 14: Bridges shall be surveyed. Article 15: The boundaries of counties, districts, townships (or districts) shall be surveyed and drawn clearly. If the boundary is a river, the opposite bank line shall also be surveyed. If it is a road or piece of land, the shape outside the boundary shall also be slightly surveyed. Article 16: For land that has been determined to be roads, ditches, embankments, or railway lines, and the construction project has started, or the construction project has not started, but the competent authority has erected a stake and submitted an actual survey map, the measurement shall be carried out according to the new land use. Article 17: If the ownership of the cliffs, banks, ridges, etc. of a piece of land is unclear, it shall be handled in accordance with the following provisions: 1. If it is between two lands of different heights, it shall belong to the higher land. 2. If it is between two lands of the same height, the center shall be the boundary. 3. It shall belong to the customary ownership. Article 18: If the upper layer of land is an embankment or road, and the lower layer of land is another type of land use, the foot of the cliff shall belong to the upper layer of land, but if there are special circumstances, or the slope of the foot of the cliff is very slow, and the boundary with the lower layer of land is unclear, it shall be measured and planned according to the shovel digging location and other areas deemed appropriate. Article 19: If the lower layer of land is a river, ditch, or road, and the upper layer of land is another type of land use, the foot of the cliff shall belong to the upper layer of land, but this shall not apply if it is deemed to belong to the lower layer of land according to the actual situation. Article 20: For adjacent residential houses of the same owner, only if they are separated by walls or other buildings, or the remaining land outside the house is small, they may be measured together. Article 21: Matters not specified in these rules may be handled with reference to the provisions of the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau's Implementation Rules for Land Survey Business in the Whole Province, which were promulgated in 1921. Article 22: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions. Article 23: These rules shall be promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau and reported to the Provincial Government for record.

(2) Valuation of Land: Valuation of land is an essential part of land administration and the foundation for construction. Dr. Sun Yat-sen specifically listed "land valuation" in the Law on the Implementation of Local Self-Government, and Article 10 of the Program for National Reconstruction also stipulates that "when each county begins self-government, it must first stipulate the price of privately owned land, and the method shall be reported by the land owner himself." Recently, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek also emphasized the urgency of levying urban land value tax to equalize the burden on the people in his address to the administrative chiefs of ten provinces in Nanchang. Therefore, land valuation is indeed one of the most important policies at present. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has promulgated the Jiangsu Provincial Urban Land Value Declaration Method, and has designated Wuxi and Nantong, two industrial and commercial cities, as the areas for initial implementation, in order to develop municipal construction and prosper industrial and commercial cities. It is heard that the land value declaration work in the two counties has been scheduled by the Provincial Government to be implemented from July 1, and the Provincial Land Bureau is actively engaged in all preparations, and the work is extremely tense. Songjiang: Water Police Arrest Suspects in Robbery of Ship 86

The Dashan area of Fengjing is located at the intersection of Songjiang, Qingpu, and Jiashan counties, and is an area where bandits often appear. On the 25th of last month, a Shenhu bus ship was passing through the area when it was suddenly ordered to stop by bandits lying in ambush. The ship attempted to speed away to avoid danger, but was forced to stop by the bandits firing guns. The bandits disembarked and looted freely, carrying away stolen goods and disappearing ashore with loud shouts. The case was jointly investigated by the water and land police, but no clues have been found so far. Now it is learned that Hu Tu, the third squad leader of the first team of the Provincial Public Security Force on the water, arrested a Chen Dongmou, a suspect related to the case, in Fengjing yesterday. He was escorted to Songjiang and transferred to the district headquarters for interrogation.
