Special Report

Impressions of the Economic Survey of Guangxi Province (Continued) 92

— Qian Jiaju

Why can Yulin homespun cloth exist? This is worth studying. In Guilin, it relies on the Hunan people's spirit of hard work, but here it relies on the clever exploitation of merchant capital. Most of the weavers here are locals, but Yulin (and the Pingnan area) has a special yarn distribution system and a yarn-for-cloth system. There are about 30 homespun cloth shops in Yulin. Some of them distribute yarn to weavers, and some exchange yarn for cloth. Those who distribute yarn to weavers usually put the yarn on the loom head in advance. Each loom head uses one strand of yarn, which can weave two bolts of cloth 3.7 feet long and 1.7 feet wide. They pay wages of 180 or 300 copper coins. Three hundred copper coins are equivalent to about 1.45 yuan in local silver. But how many days does it take to weave 10 bolts of cloth? The most diligent person takes 12 days, and a slow person takes half a month. Earning 1.45 yuan in half a month is really not enough to maintain the minimum standard of living. Another system is to exchange yarn for cloth, usually at a flat rate. The best is to exchange two pounds of cloth for one jin and two liang of yarn. No wages are paid. Why are some weavers willing to do flat exchange (i.e., two pounds of cloth for two pounds of yarn)? Because the cloth is usually starched to make it stiff. Usually, every jin of cloth has three or four liang of rice paste. Therefore, although it is said to be a flat exchange, there are three or four liang of rice paste in one jin of cloth, while two jin of yarn is unstarched yarn. The weavers rely on earning a few liang of yarn in this rice paste. This is the only price of their labor. But rice paste also costs money, so the yarn-for-cloth system is even more miserable than the yarn distribution system. At the same time, the yarn shops are very picky about the cloth they weave. If the size or weight is slightly different, they refuse to accept it under various excuses. The weavers have to endure all the harsh conditions with tears in their eyes. We ourselves have witnessed this situation more than once. This cruel sweatshop system can only exist in China, where the feudal economy dominates. This is really more terrible than the exploitation of workers by British factory owners described by Marx in the first volume of Capital. But Yulin yarn merchants should get a lot of profit through such exploitation. In fact, according to our calculations, it is also extremely pitiful. The selling price of Yulin homespun cloth, which is 15 yards long and 1.7 feet wide, is 2.23 yuan per bolt. The cost of weaving one bolt of cloth requires about four and two-thirds of the 20-count yarn. The local market price of 20-count yarn is 288 yuan per package, and the price of each strand is 3.6 cents. Plus the grinding labor, yarn pulling labor, pigments, paper materials, etc., each bolt costs about 50 cents, totaling more than 2.1 yuan. Therefore, each bolt of cloth earns at most one or two dimes. This again proves that after capitalist commodities invade the poor countryside of China, even if the indigenous family industry of China does not fall into complete bankruptcy, it can only live out its remnant life in such a miserable environment.

Xinding Village in Yulin (about 10 miles from the city) is one of the central areas of the weaving industry. There is a Mr. Li Zenong here, who is worth special mention. This Mr. Li (the villagers call him Teacher Li Shisi) has never been to school, and has never studied mechanical engineering, but he has accumulated more than 20 years of experience and has automatically invented a loom that can weave 16 to 24 candlewick strips at the same time. According to him, if it is enlarged, it can weave three bolts of cloth at the same time. This machine is made of wood, mixed with simple mechanical principles. While weaving the belt, it can also spin yarn. One person only needs to step on the bottom with their feet, without the need for hand movements. According to his own account of the process of inventing the machine, he only saw iron-made towel machines being imported into the local area for the first time during the Xuan Tong years. Later, because the towels were not suitable for the times, they were changed to weaving cloth (during the 7th and 8th years of the Republic of China). By the 21st year of the Republic of China, because the sales of cloth were not very good, they were changed to weaving belts. At first, each machine only wove two strips, then increased to four strips, from four strips to eight strips, twelve strips, and even sixteen strips today. In the future, it will not be difficult to change to weaving twenty-four strips. This machine only needs to be powered by feet, so it can be changed to hydraulic power. Unfortunately, there is no such opportunity at present. But Mr. Li is unwilling to pass on this machine to others, and also prohibits everyone in his family from visiting it. He is afraid that others will learn it, which will cause him to lose this patent opportunity (now he uses this machine he invented to weave belts, and he can earn six yuan every three days). We only took a look at it because we were introduced by a friend. In fact, the structure of the loom is also very simple, but it is a composite of three simple operating machines. We say that unfortunately, Mr. Li was born in 20th century China. If he was born in 18th century England, the status of James Hargreaves or the barber Richard Arkwright would not have been created in this way? However, he is also fortunate to be born in the remote Guangxi. If it were in Shanghai or Tianjin, where the machine industry is developed, this simple machine would definitely not allow him to have a net income of two yuan per day.

Yulin's wharf is the hub connecting Guangdong and Beihai, and it is also a place where salt and rice gather. The rice from Yulin is transported to Guangdong via the wharf, and the salt from Qinlian, Guangdong enters Guangxi via the wharf. This is also the most active place for merchant capital. In particular, the rice from several counties under Yulin gathers here. The wharf has more than ten grain and rice storage shops (there were more than 30 in the 14th and 15th years of the Republic of China). The one that collects the most rice collects and stores 2 million catties every year, and the one that collects the least also collects hundreds of thousands of catties. The peak period for buying rice is around October of the lunar calendar, which is the time when the late rice is harvested. The price of each dan of rice is about five yuan, but it rises to ten yuan per dan in April of the following year, which is the time when the old and new crops are not connected. Therefore, there is a saying in Yulin, "Poor people sell cheap rice and eat expensive rice." Of course, this is not only the case in Yulin, we are just giving an example.

Fumian Village, 30 miles away from Yulin, is another famous homespun cloth area in Yulin. It is not known for sure why it is named "Fumian," but the elders there can all say that it grew a lot of cotton around the end of the Guangxu reign. It is said that at that time, Guangdong people bought cotton in Beiliu and made it into cotton strips that were a foot long and as thick as fingers, and sold the cotton strips to farmers to spin into fine yarn. At that time, Guangxi people used this indigenous yarn to weave homespun cloth, but since the import of foreign yarn, no one has bought the cotton here again, and the number of people growing cotton has also decreased day by day. The name "Fumian" is not true. In the past, a lot of peanuts were also grown here, but since the import of kerosene, the raw oil made from peanuts has no sales, so the production of peanuts has also decreased (now they have changed to growing fluffy peanuts, which are small and fat, and are not the same as before). From these two facts, the impact of cheap capitalist commodities on the Chinese countryside can be imagined.

After leaving Yulin, we set off for Guixian. Guixian is located in the middle reaches of the West River, and is the only way to transport by water and land to Wuzhou. In addition to the fast轮 passing through here, there are also many tugboats sailing between Guixian and Wuzhou. This kind of tugboat has a large area, shallow draft, and is built in the same way as civilian ships. As long as a small gasoline boat is used to tow it in front, it can travel at the same speed as a steamship. This is a powerful tool for freight transport in Guangxi Province. Therefore, Guixian is a very important transshipment wharf in the shipping industry. Goods from neighboring counties are concentrated here and transported to Wuzhou. Goods from Wuzhou are also distributed inland through Guixian. At the same time, Guixian is also a very famous area for sugar production, and a lot of livestock are also transported out. Due to these reasons, the finance of Guixian is particularly active, and it has also become a county with a surplus of exports, which can be said to be rare in Guangxi. We only stayed in Guixian for one night, and set off for Binyang the next day.

Page 11

Local News

Executive Yuan Approves and Promulgates Fundamental Measures to Save the Silk Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang: Detailed Steps for Mulberry Planting, Seed Breeding, Cocoon Drying, and Silk Reeling; Improving Trade and Establishing Credit, Production, and Marketing Cooperatives 93

The fundamental measures to save the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, which were drafted by the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Finance, have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The full text was officially promulgated by the Ministry of Industry yesterday. The content includes extremely detailed instructions on the guidance of mulberry trees by technical personnel, the technical improvement of silkworms and the ban on the use of poor seeds, the improvement of silk management and the formulation of silk industry regulations, as well as the investigation of the amount of silk needed abroad, the establishment of cooperatives, and the training of technical personnel. The following is the full text recorded by the New Voice News Agency reporter stationed in Beijing.

Encouraging Mulberry Planting 94

(I) Mulberry Trees (A) Encouraging the Planting of Mulberry Trees in New Areas: The provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are both suitable for sericulture. Areas where silkworm rearing is underdeveloped should be urgently encouraged to plant mulberry trees, so as to directly increase the production of mulberry leaves and indirectly promote the increase of silk production. As for ways to encourage, in addition to the central government formulating incentive regulations, the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should currently provide excellent mulberry seedlings to farmers free of charge or at low prices, or include a certain amount of silk industry incentive funds in the annual provincial budget to subsidize this expense. At the same time, the cultivation of seedlings should also be encouraged, so that the source of mulberry seedlings is abundant. (B) Guiding Farmers to Improve Mulberry Orchards: Improving mulberry orchards is the fundamental key to managing the silk industry. Measures such as replanting abandoned mulberry orchards, popularizing superior varieties, establishing dedicated mulberry orchards, establishing young silkworm mulberry orchards, improving cultivation methods, improving fertilizers, and preventing and controlling diseases and pests should be implemented by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, who should dispatch their affiliated sericulture technicians to provide on-site guidance. In addition, the promotion of silkworm rearing with self-produced mulberry leaves and the ban on bad habits in mulberry leaf trading should also be earnestly implemented to thoroughly rationalize mulberry orchard management.

Guiding Silkworm Rearing 95

(II) Silkworms (A) Prohibiting Farmers from Using Inferior Silkworm Eggs: At present, farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces still use homemade local silkworm eggs for silkworm rearing. These local eggs are of mixed quality and carry many viruses. The inferiority of these eggs is a major obstacle to the progress of the entire silk industry. For thorough improvement, the construction departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should supervise and order all counties to prohibit farmers from purchasing and rearing local eggs. They should be instructed to purchase improved varieties or be provided with them free of charge by the government. At the same time, those who produce local eggs should be gradually guided and taught new methods to match the techniques of improved egg production farms. Furthermore, improved egg-producing merchants should not be allowed to take advantage of the situation, arbitrarily raising egg prices to seek profit. This method should be overseen by the silk industry regulatory offices of the two provinces. The implementation steps should be carried out by year and by region, so that the quantity of improved eggs will not run short in practice. B. Hoping that Farmers Will Improve Silkworm Rearing Techniques: Although Jiangsu and Zhejiang are developed sericultural areas, farmers' silkworm rearing techniques still adhere to old methods and are stagnant. Even with excellent silkworm eggs, the results still end in failure. Therefore, methods such as disinfection, hatching, feeding, and mounting should be earnestly guided by the construction departments of the two provinces by region to improve silkworm rearing techniques and achieve the effect of upgrading raw silk quality. C. Promoting Autumn Silkworm Rearing: The construction departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should supervise and urge construction sections of all counties to earnestly encourage farmers to rear autumn silkworms in order to utilize equipment, balance labor, promote the rural economy, and increase silk production.

Improving Silkworm Eggs 96

(III) Silkworm Eggs A. Unifying Silkworm Breeds: To improve the quality of raw silk, it is necessary to improve and sort the raw material cocoons. The root of improving and sorting raw material cocoons lies in unifying silkworm breeds. Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should designate several breeds with superior performance from the currently used spring and autumn breeds for rearing, so that silk cocoons can be unified. At the same time, efforts should be made to test and verify them in order to discover more appropriate silkworm breeds for adoption. B. Rewarding High-Performing Egg Farms and Shutting Down Unreasonable Egg Farms: For egg farms with complete equipment, exquisite technology, and excellent products, the construction departments of the two provinces should allocate a portion of the silk industry incentive funds to subsidize them. Egg farms with simple equipment and crude manufacturing should be strictly shut down in accordance with regulations in order to promote the development of the silkworm egg industry.

Using Cocoon Drying Machines 97

(IV) Cocoons (A) Cocoon Trading: The principle should be direct trade between farmers and silk mills. In the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai areas, the cocoons used by silk mills often cannot be purchased directly from farmers and are often bought and sold by cocoon merchants in the middle, causing the silk cocoons to increase in price. From now on, the construction departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should formulate and announce cocoon collection methods. Anyone wishing to collect cocoons must comply with these methods. (B) Encourage the Adoption of New-Style Cocoon Drying Machines and Ban Newly Established Old-Style Soil Stove Cocoon Drying: Old-style soil stove cocoon drying often deteriorates good cocoons, increasing the silk reel breakage and degrading the quality. From now on, the use of new-style cocoon drying machines should be encouraged, and old-style soil stoves should be banned. The methods are as follows: (1) Farmers who use cooperative methods to install new-style cocoon drying machines will be granted a considerable incentive by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces (the amount to be determined by the two provinces themselves), or the construction departments of the two provinces will guarantee to borrow up to half of the equipment costs from the bank; (2) If silk merchants want to install or improve new-style cocoon drying machines, they can also apply to the provincial construction department for a guarantee to borrow a certain amount of equipment costs from the bank; (3) During the cocoon collection season, technical personnel from the construction department will go to various places to guide new-style mechanical cocoon drying technology; (4) Newly established cocoon collection and drying institutions that still use old-style soil stoves should be strictly banned.

Improving Silk Reeling 98

(V) Silk: The reasons for the losses of silk mills in the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai areas are partly due to temporary fluctuations in the silk market exchange rate, but poor internal management, inadequate management, and outdated machinery are indeed fundamental and important reasons. The improvement methods are described below: (A) Formulate Regulations on the Silk Industry: The central government should formulate and promulgate regulations on the silk industry to ban inferior silk mills; (B) Guide Silk Mills to Improve Management Methods: Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should send personnel to various factories from time to time to guide manufacturers in the rational operation of raw material purchases, raw silk sales, and other aspects; (C) Encourage the Adoption of Appropriate Machinery that Can Improve Quality and Reduce Costs: For silk manufacturers who want to adopt new-style appropriate cocoon cooking, silk reeling, inspection, and other machinery, the government should provide incentives. The method is for silk manufacturers to apply to the provincial construction department for a guarantee to borrow up to one-third of the equipment costs from the bank; (D) Guide Silk Mills to Improve Silk Making Technology: The construction departments of the two provinces should send technical personnel to guide various factories from time to time to carry out rational mechanical cocoon cooking, fixed denier or single cocoon, variable silk reeling, silk winding, and rational operation of silk adding, and other technologies that should be improved, such as silk graduallly slowed down, silk reeling end counts are increased. Other techniques that should be improved, such as finishing and inspection, should also be guided in order to manufacture excellent products that meet standards; (E) Guide Silk Mills to Implement Rational Management: The construction departments of the two provinces should send technical personnel to guide various factories from time to time to carry out rational supervision of work, attention to employee hygiene, and fair treatment, so as to encourage all personnel in the factory to work together wholeheartedly and to promote the prosperity of the enterprise and share benefits between labor and capital.

Raw Silk Trade 99

(VI) Raw Silk Trade: (A) Implement Direct Export Through Official-Merchant Cooperation and Overseas Promotion: The Chinese silk trade has always been in the hands of foreign merchants. Even Chinese merchants who are engaged in it have weak capital and no means of promotion. Except for Tongyun, the rest have successively announced their closure. From now on, the central government and the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should cooperate with silk manufacturers and the financial community to organize a Chinese silk promotion company (the head office should be located in Shanghai, and sales offices should be established in New York, Lyon, London, and India) to directly export and sell Chinese silk and to investigate overseas demand and market price fluctuations, report to domestic silk manufacturers, and promote the advantages of Chinese silk overseas; (B) Implement Raw Silk Inspection and Graded Sales: Chinese silk has never been graded, and overseas purchasers often suffer from a lack of uniform standards. From now on, the silk produced by each factory should be sent to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau for strict inspection and grading. Raw silk should be sold on the spot or in futures according to its inspection grade, eliminating the past practice of relying solely on futures sales.

Organize Cooperatives 100

(VII) Sericulture Cooperatives: (A) Guide People to Organize Credit Cooperatives: From mulberry planting and silkworm rearing to raw silk trading, the sericulture industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang feels the difficulty of financial circulation, especially in rural areas. From now on, the governments of the two provinces should send personnel to supervise and order their subordinates to guide people to organize various credit cooperatives in order to promote financial circulation, or organize various credit cooperatives such as mulberry planting and silkworm rearing based on business scope, or organize sericulture credit cooperatives in a certain province, county, or area based on region. These cooperatives can apply to the provincial construction department for a guarantee to borrow low-interest long-term loans from the bank; (B) Guide People to Organize Production, Sales, and Transportation Cooperatives: Production, sales, and transportation cooperatives and credit cooperatives are equally important measures for improving the silk industry at present. From now on, the construction departments of the two provinces should supervise and instruct all counties to guide people to organize various production, sales, and transportation cooperatives, or organize production cooperatives such as silkworm rearing, refrigeration, and cocoon drying, and cocoon and silk purchasing, transportation and sales cooperatives based on business scope, or organize production, sales, and transportation cooperatives in a certain province, county, or area based on region.

Experiment and Research 101

(VIII) Experiment and Research on Various Issues in the Silk Industry: There are many aspects that need to be experimented and researched. Based on the current equipment situation of various institutions, a division of labor and cooperation method should be adopted. Various experiments and research on silkworm, mulberry, and egg varieties should be undertaken by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, the United Sericulture Improvement Association, the Jiangsu Sericulture Experiment Station, the Yangzhou Original Silkworm Egg Production Station, and the Zhejiang Agricultural Improvement General Station Sericulture Station. Various experiments and research on cocoons and silk should be undertaken by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, the Zhejiang Agricultural Improvement General Station, and the Hangzhou Silk Factory.

Cultivate Talent 102

(IX) The Cultivation and Improvement of Sericulture Technical Talent: The above-mentioned fundamental improvement work requires various technical talents for its practical implementation, and there must be farmers with sericulture technology to drive it. Therefore, the cultivation and improvement of sericulture technical talent is indeed an urgent matter at present. The methods are as follows: A. The Central Government Establishes an Advanced Sericulture Technical Personnel Training Institute: The central government selects an appropriate location to establish an advanced specialized technical personnel training institute, divided into sericulture and silk making departments, to train advanced technical talents. B. Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Establish Farmers' Sericulture Training Institutes: The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces each establish a mobile sericulture training institute to teach farmers the necessary knowledge and experience in mulberry planting, silkworm rearing, and egg production. C. Establish a Sericulture Research Association: The central government hires sericulture experts from various places to undertake various research work on silk. When necessary, the central government may convene experts to discuss it. D. Hold Sericulture Training Courses: Sericulture institutions of the central government and Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces hold sericulture training courses in various places from time to time to teach farmers simple and necessary sericulture knowledge and experience.

Reduce and Exempt Taxes 103

(X) Propose to Reduce or Exempt Taxes and Freight on Cocoons and Silk to Promote the Development of the Silk Industry: A. Propose that the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces issue orders to their subordinates to appropriately reduce various local silk taxes. B. Propose that the Railway and Communications Departments find ways to appropriately reduce freight rates for mulberry seedlings and silk cocoons. (XI) Control of the Silk Industry: When the central government and the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces deem it necessary to control various undertakings such as mulberry, silkworm, egg, and silk production, they may implement various controls.

However, the entry procedures are difficult, there is a lack of managers, and there are few ships traveling between China and South Africa, so trade with South Africa is greatly restricted and should be improved urgently. In recent years, due to the surplus of domestic agricultural products, it is eager to open up markets in the Far East to develop foreign trade. It has specially sent Mr. Burns, a commercial commissioner stationed in the UK, to the Far East to exchange opinions with local authorities and enhance business relations. He has also come to China to inspect everything. China and South Africa may be able to use this to improve the business relations between the two countries to develop trade with South Africa.

This Year It Is Planned to Expand to Two Hundred Warehouses, With Estimated Storage and Pledges of Three Million Yuan

The Jiangsu Farmers Bank has been operating for five years and has always paid close attention to the storage and pledge business, and has made considerable progress. This year's wheat and beans have been harvested, and although it is said that there is hope for a bumper harvest, the price of wheat is expected to fall. At the same time, after the rice harvest, prices will inevitably decline naturally. Therefore, those with outstanding warehouse achievements have specially inquired about the warehouse storage and pledge situation from the bank. The following is recorded for the reference of those who are concerned about the rural economy.

Warehouse Situation 107

The bank is the only regulatory agency for the rural economy in Jiangsu Province. Since its establishment, in addition to providing loans to farmers for necessary production funds, it has devoted itself to the operation of agricultural product warehouse storage and pledges, hoping to use this to activate the entire rural finance in Jiangsu Province. Therefore, promoting warehouse storage and pledges is an important policy of the bank. At present, the bank has ninety-five storage and pledge warehouses that it operates itself and entrusts to agents. The bank's branches operate thirty-eight warehouses themselves, and entrust local organizations

Following Zhang Gongquan's Return from Sichuan, Zhang Xiaomei Talks About Her Impressions of the Inspection; Investment by the Bank of China Is Difficult to Determine at This Time 108

According to the Dagong News Agency, Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China, in order to develop the resources of the interior, circulate the rural economy, and develop industry, specially went to Sichuan Province last month with Zhang Xiaomei, Director of the Bank's Economic Research Group, and Shi Jiu'ao, Deputy Manager of the Bank, to conduct on-site inspections and inspect the affairs of the Bank's Sichuan branch. After more than a month, they returned to Shanghai by boat the day before yesterday. Yesterday afternoon, a reporter from the Dagong News Agency specifically went to the Bank of China to visit, but there were so many visitors that he did not have time to meet him. He specially instructed Secretary Ji of the Bank to tell the reporter that General Manager Zhang intends to draft an article within a day or two to present his findings from this inspection to all sectors. Later, the reporter asked to see Zhang Xiaomei, Director of the Economic Research Group, who accompanied Zhang to Sichuan, and she agreed to meet him. The following is a record of her impressions of the trip to Sichuan.

The Task of the Trip to Sichuan Was to Inspect the Branches 109

According to Zhang Xiaomei, the task of General Manager Zhang and herself on this trip to Sichuan was to inspect the branches in various places, although it was also to inspect the industry in the interior. The Sichuan branch has been established for more than twenty years, and due to various political factors, it has rarely communicated with the head office. At present, the military affairs in Sichuan have come to an end, and the twenty-first year has become a unified situation. Therefore, he made a special trip to Sichuan to inspect the recent situation of the branches in order to make some adjustments.

Backward Production and Import Surplus 110

Sichuan Province is known as the Land of Abundance, rich and unparalleled, and can be self-sufficient without relying on foreign goods. The land is fertile and can grow various agricultural products. If the political situation is clear, why would the people not be able to make a living? Unfortunately, in the past, warlords fought for territory, and wars continued for years, resulting in bandits everywhere, rural bankruptcy, and a gradual decline in the goods exported and an increase in the goods imported in recent years due to backward industries. A surplus province has become an import surplus province. When our colleagues arrived in Sichuan, it happened to be the time when the provincial authorities held a production conference to discuss relief measures. However, these relief measures were limited to one corner and could not be planned comprehensively, so the effectiveness was probably minimal. Our colleagues arrived when the conference was about to close, so they were unable to participate, but the military and political authorities of Sichuan Province met with them at this time.

Political and Military Affairs Are Gradually Becoming Unified 111

Mr. Liu Fuchen, Chairman of Sichuan Province, is extremely intelligent and capable and works hard on local construction. Unfortunately, he has not taken a step out of the door and has little contact with the outside world. He is inevitably isolated from the trends of the world, and he seems to be slightly unclear about the national situation in China. Mr. Tang Dihai, Director of the Department of Finance, is also very concerned about organizing the finances of Sichuan Province. The reason why it has not been able to unify with the central government is that there are various obstacles in the local system. However, politics is gradually getting on track, and military affairs are gradually becoming unified. This is also a good phenomenon in Sichuan Province.

Heavy Taxes and Chaotic Currency System 112

Sichuan Province has the largest number of soldiers among the provinces, so the financial authorities have to increase heavy taxes to cope with this huge military expenditure, which has led to industrialists not being able to bear the burden and closing down one after another, and investors are competing to stop, creating opportunities for the import of foreign goods. For example, the tax on a dozen toothbrushes used to be 3 cents, but now it has increased to 2 dimes, which shows the severity of the taxes. Furthermore, the currency system is chaotic, almost unparalleled. The use of copper coins even changes from place to place, and the suffering of the people is unspeakable. However, the currency system is closely related to the financial community, and the financial community should assist in reforming it to eliminate local malpractices.

Goods Abandoned on the Ground Need to be Exploited 113

Sichuan Province has a mild climate and abundant products. The annual production of salt from Zigong, sugarcane from Neijiang, and white wax and silk from Jiading is unlimited. Unfortunately, they adhere to old methods, do not know how to improve, resulting in waste of raw materials and reduced production. The method of making salt in Zigong is to dig a few feet into the soil with artificial labor, take out large bamboo tubes to draw out the salt quality, and do not use sunlight to dry it. Dig deep into the ground again, wait for the gas to gush out and burn it with fire. It relies on the gas to dry it, because the underground there contains extremely rich coal quality. For example, sugarcane in Neijiang is ground into juice with cows and donkeys, and then sugar is fried with firewood. Those who use machines to manufacture are as rare as phoenix feathers. The labor of a whole day and night is still not equal to the power of a machine for twenty minutes, which is a pity. For example, tung oil is also a very large product of Sichuan. In the past, Yichang was the meeting place, and it was operated exclusively by the Zhongyuan Company, which has also declared its failure recently. The coal in Sichuan is also a very large resource. At this moment, no one has exploited it, resulting in goods being abandoned on the ground.

Investment by the Bank of China Is Difficult to Determine at This Time 114

As for the rumors that the purpose of General Manager Zhang's trip to Sichuan was to study the goal of investment, this cannot be discussed at this time. For the sake of its own interests, the Bank of China does not directly operate its investment. It must consider whether the politics of each place is on track and whether the local authorities can cooperate sincerely is the most important key. If politics is not on the right track, if someone sets up a very large factory in the interior and is taxed very heavily, would entrepreneurs dare to invest under such circumstances? Therefore, the Bank of China's investment in Sichuan Province is still difficult to determine.

The Scenery is Beautiful and the Best in the World 115

The places that our colleagues visited were first from Shanghai to Hankou, where they stayed briefly to inspect the Hankou branch, then from Hankou to Yichang, from Yichang to Wanxian, and then to Chongqing, Chengdu, Zigong, and Neijiang. Recently, from Neijiang to Jiading was the end point. Because we passed Mount Emei, we visited the scenery and stayed for a few days, and then we went directly east. The impression of this trip is that the scenery in Sichuan is unforgettable for us. The mountains in Sichuan are surrounded by mountains and rivers, and the scenery is the best in the world. Compared with Switzerland in Europe and the West, it is even better. Switzerland has a very narrow width and a small production, but it can use the quiet beauty of the scenery to attract foreign investment and maintain its national expenses. If Sichuan is developed, its politics are stable, its construction is perfect, and its transportation is convenient, all sectors of the country will inevitably rise up and enter Sichuan in the future, and the limits of its development are unlimited.

The Three Gorges, North Fu, and the Land of Peach Blossoms 116

Ms. Zhang finally told the reporter cautiously that there is also a place in the Three Gorges that is not related to military affairs, politics, and financial conditions, but has a very close relationship with education. It is truly a blessed place in Sichuan, no less than a land of peach blossoms. It is found that the North Fu area of the Three Gorges used to be a bandit area. After Yang Sen's recovery, Mr. Lu Zuofu, General Manager of the Minsheng Shipping Company, exhausted his efforts to operate it. The annual funding required is about 60,000 yuan. If the local production is not enough, Mr. Lu will subsidize it. There is a spirited and well-equipped militia to defend the local area, and there is a perfect educational institution to enlighten the people. The facilities such as instrument halls, libraries, hospitals, research rooms, hygiene halls, schools, factories, as well as improved teahouses, improved theaters, etc., are all available. The cleanliness of the roads and the neatness of the layout are unparalleled in all parts of the country. In the prosperous world of ancient times, those who did not pick up things lost on the road and did not close their doors at night seemed to be like it.

There are thirty-two agencies, and twenty-five are run by cooperatives or farmers' education halls, distributed in more than twenty counties with abundant agricultural products such as Suzhou, Changzhou, Wuxi, Danyang, Jiangyin, Wujiang, Qingpu, Xuzhou, Yancheng, and Rugao, specializing in the storage and pledge of agricultural products near the county to regulate agricultural prices and benefit the turnover of rural finance.

Storage and Pledge Quantity 117

The bank has ninety-five storage and pledge warehouses that it operates itself and entrusts to agents. The quantity of various agricultural products stored and pledged this year has reached more than 500,443 dan, and the total value of storage and pledges is more than 1.28 million yuan. At this time when the rural economy is bankrupt and financial turnover is sluggish, this huge amount of funds is distributed in the rural areas of various counties. Although it has not been able to restore and prosper the rural economy in one fell swoop, the financial activities and turnover in rural areas have indeed been far better than in the past.

Statistics by Category 118

Our nation is founded on agriculture, and the main agricultural products are rice, grains, beans, wheat, miscellaneous grains, silk, cotton, and bean cakes. Jiangsu Province is located on the coast of the East Sea, with the Yangtze River running through the middle and the Grand Canal flowing vertically from north to south. Its abundance of water conservancy far surpasses that of other provinces, so these kinds of agricultural products are especially rich. However, due to the drastic drop in prices, rural villages are increasingly becoming bankrupt. This bank, regarding the agricultural products of various counties in Jiangsu Province, such as rice, grains, beans, wheat, raw silk, bean cakes, and cotton, has been storing and mortgaging them to the greatest extent possible. According to statistics from the bank's own and entrusted agency warehouses, the agricultural products currently stored and mortgaged are most abundant in rice and grains, followed by beans, wheat, bean cakes, cotton, and raw silk. The quantity stored and mortgaged this year is estimated at approximately 250,000 *shi* of rice and grains, approximately 30,000 *shi* of wheat, approximately 30,000 *shi* of beans, approximately 20,000 *shi* of cotton, approximately 100,000 pieces of bean cakes, approximately 20,000 *shi* of miscellaneous grains, approximately 8,000 *shi* of raw silk, approximately 1,500 *shi* of fertilizer powder, and approximately 30,000 bolts of cloth.

Expansion Plan 119

It is heard that in addition to expanding the existing warehouses in various counties, the bank has now decided to continue adding more to strive for promotion. It also plans to handle storage and mortgage matters on behalf of the agricultural warehouse management committees of various counties. It is estimated that within this year, 2 million *dan* of rice and grains will be mortgaged, with 3 million yuan used as storage and mortgage funds. In terms of rescuing the entire rural economy, its effect may not be very significant, but compared to the situation last year, it should be a considerable increase in effect.

Wu Kai-xian and Chen Ke-cheng Telegraph the Provincial Government

Thoroughly Investigate the Qingpu Lantern Ban Dispute. Provoked Public Outrage, Created Chaos in the Market. Should Be Strictly Investigated According to Law 128

In Zhujiajiao Town, Qingpu County, the district chief, Wang Rongzhong, for no reason, banned the carrying of lanterns, which provoked public outrage. The district chief still did not repent, but arbitrarily ordered the arrest of good citizens, creating chaos in the market. Fellow villagers of the county in Shanghai, Wu Kaixian and Chen Kecheng, telegraphed the provincial government, requesting a thorough investigation to punish the lawless. The text is as follows: We have learned that in Zhujiajiao Town, in the second district of Qingpu County, the party and government organs of the town, in order to promote the New Life Movement, initially led all sectors to hold a propaganda conference on April 21st and 22nd. Later, the people of all sectors, in order to expand propaganda, held a lantern parade on May 29th, 30th, and 31st, so that the main purpose of the New Life Movement could penetrate the people. Considering that all major cities in the country have similar actions, this move by the town should not be inappropriate. However, when the town held the third day of the lantern parade on the evening of the 31st, the town's district chief, Wang Yingzhong, suddenly telegraphed the first branch of the Public Security Bureau for no reason, dispatched police to stop it, and detained lanterns, intending to forcibly dissolve the parade. The merchants and residents of the town, because the matter was unexpected, were suspicious and outraged, resulting in the unfortunate dispute of destroying the Public Security Bureau branch, the district office, and the private residence of the district chief. All that has happened, please examine it carefully. Kecheng and others are traveling in Shanghai, deeply concerned about their hometown, pitying the people's will being suppressed, justice being difficult to achieve, and especially fearing that it will cause great changes and endanger the local area. What the heart feels is dangerous and difficult to silence, sincerely presented to you. Zhujiajiao connects Zhejiang and Jiangsu, with merchants gathered from all over. It was originally the most important town in Qingpu County. In recent years, the country has been in turmoil, and all industries have declined. Now, the merchants and residents of the town held a lantern festival, in order to promote the New Life Movement, and also to revive the market, and to allow merchants and farmers to relieve their accumulated depression after a year of fatigue. This is both reasonable and appropriate. However, the district chief, Wang Yingzhong, as the district chief, was not aware of the suffering of the people, let alone the proposal for the lantern festival. Moreover, the 29th and 30th had already been approved and held in an orderly manner, so why did he suddenly ban it on the 31st? Even if the district chief had other opinions on the lantern festival, why not stop it beforehand, but wait until two days after it was held before banning it? The reason for this is difficult to understand. District Chief Wang Yingzhong is usually clumsy, which is enough to see one aspect of this. This is one. On the 31st, the district chief temporarily telegraphed the Public Security Bureau to dispatch police to stop the lantern festival, and when the people were agitated and outraged and went to question, he was unable to explain himself and only knew how to threaten with dangerous words, even pulling out a box cannon, intending to fire it. Fortunately, it was seized and no major disaster occurred. District Chief Wang Yingzhong's misconduct is self-evident. This is two. The lantern festival was prepared in advance, costing both time and money. Being banned for no reason on the 31st, it is unavoidable to feel resentment in light of common sense. The people of the town were unable to restrain their feelings, and they were not calm when the incident occurred, thus destroying public property. Considering human feelings and the law, it is also understandable. However, the district chief falsely accused the higher authorities after the incident, arbitrarily framing others, personally leading the police, holding Browning pistols, and indiscriminately arresting good citizens in large numbers, as many as thirty or forty people. He also used private torture and forced confessions, and declared that anyone who participated in the lantern festival would be arrested. How can our villagers bear it? District Chief Wang Yingzhong arbitrarily acted recklessly, exploiting the common people, not only tarnishing the official code, but also violating discipline. This shows that he did not regret the disaster afterwards. This is three. Furthermore, Wang Yingzhong, as the head of the local autonomous region, caused the lantern festival dispute in the district, which is enough to show the lack of training of the people by the district chief. If he cannot govern himself, how can he govern others? Thinking of this, it is painful to speak. It is heard that the arrested people are shackled and imprisoned, treated like thieves, and after being shocked by heavy punishment, some are mentally disturbed or seriously injured. It is also heard that the county government has recently issued arrest warrants, summoning the executive committee members of the chamber of commerce, Long Ji-liang, Jin Hai-dong, Zhang Qiu-chen, etc., causing panic in the whole town and fear among the villagers, who are mostly reluctant to move forward. The market is becoming increasingly depressed, and they are restless all day long. Considering this situation, it is deeply shocking. I believe that the incident in the town was entirely caused by the district chief, Wang Yingzhong, and the arrested people, whether farmers or merchants, are all law-abiding citizens. Although their actions may have been excessive, they were forced by circumstances and provoked by public outrage. Forgive their ignorance, it does not seem appropriate to be harsh. If it is said that there is another background and an attempt to riot, then it is easy to add guilt. As for the executive committee members of the chamber of commerce, they are related to the prosperity and decline of the local area. You are all known to be people of integrity and just gentlemen in the area. Today, this unprovoked summons will inevitably fundamentally shake the entire town's commerce and finance. Unless it is necessary to make the entire town miserable before feeling satisfied, it must be a deliberate attempt to implicate others, which is also inappropriate. I have always admired your compassion for the people's suffering, treating the people as if they were injured. I dare to sincerely request that you examine the facts and instruct the Qingpu County government to handle the case leniently, and promptly order District Chief Wang Yingzhong to be escorted to the province for strict punishment, and select competent personnel to take over, in order to maintain the people's lives and ensure peace. The telegraph is urgent, and I am extremely frightened and await orders.

It is also reported that the town's chamber of commerce telegraphed the provincial government's Chairman Chen and Commissioner Yu the day before yesterday, saying: Zhujiajiao Town in the second district of Qingpu County, since all the organs and organizations were ordered to initiate the New Life Movement lantern parade, the local people, in order to expand the propaganda, continued to carry lanterns and ended the parade on May 29th to 31st, carrying lanterns during the day for three days. Unexpectedly, at 1 pm on the 31st, just as the lanterns were being assembled, District Chief Wang Shi-xiu suddenly telegraphed Jin, a member of the Public Security Bureau, to dispatch police to stop the parade (at that time, the branch chief Yao Yu was on leave due to business), which angered the people. The crowd was so large that the Public Security Bureau branch was destroyed. Then, the police officers of the Public Security Bureau stated that the lantern ban was requested by District Chief Wang Shi-xiu. The crowd swarmed to the district office, the entertainment venue, and Wang Shi-xiu's residence, destroying everything and dispersing in a flurry. This time, violating the New Life Movement and causing a major change, District Chief Wang Shi-xiu is truly to blame. Instead of reflecting on himself, he was stubborn and used money to falsely accuse County Chief Qian, arbitrarily framing others, personally leading the police, and indiscriminately arresting good citizens, such as the executive committee members, Jun Liang and Jin Hai-dong, and member Zhang Qiu-chen, who are all wealthy and law-abiding citizens. Everyone in the area knows this, and they are also falsely accused. In this way, human rights lose their guarantee, and what is the meaning of the rule of law? Moreover, one wave has not subsided, and another wave has risen. Suddenly, on the evening of the 6th of this month, the district chief and all the chiefs and police officers of the Public Security Bureau had a major dispute, which almost caused a catastrophe, causing panic among the people and several shocks in one night. If it is not resolved quickly, the consequences will be dire. In addition to submitting separate reports to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs and the Qingpu County Government, we are urgently telegraphing you, requesting you to send a senior official to thoroughly investigate and severely punish the troublemakers, in order to maintain human rights. It would be fortunate for the local area and fortunate for the merchants and people. Gao Huan-chang, Chairman of the Zhujiajiao Town Chamber of Commerce in Qingpu County, bows.

Statistics of Chinese Goods Exported to the United States in April 142

According to the Great American Evening News, the U.S. Consul General in Shanghai issued statistics stating that in April this year, Chinese exports to the United States, excluding Hong Kong, were worth US$3,516,845. The total for the first four months of this year was US$17,651,428. Non-edible animals and animal products accounted for the first place, with US$1,766,338 in April and US$8,892,916 in the four months combined. Textiles were second, with US$768,728 in April and US$4,673,395 in the four months combined. Non-edible plant products were third, with US$384,547 in April and US$2,018,832 in the four months combined. Metals and metal products were fourth, with US$225,262 in April and US$588,238 in the four months combined. Plant foods and beverages were fifth, with US$156,305 in April and US$671,108 in the four months combined. The other categories varied in quantity. In addition, silver and silver coins exported to the United States in April were worth US$307,476, and the total for the four months was US$830,733.

Zhang Jingou Talks – Land Reclamation and Locust Control are More Effective – Practical Politics to Relieve Farmers' Suffering 149

In view of the locust plague, which occurs every year and directly harms the farmers' economy, the Ministry of Industry held a seven-province locust control conference in Beijing. The representative from the Commodity Inspection Bureau of this city was Zhang Jingou, director of the Pest Control Department. The conference closed on the 7th of this month, and Mr. Zhang also returned to Shanghai a few days ago. The reporter specially went to inquire about the proceedings of the conference and what his impressions were. The main points of Mr. Zhang's reply are recorded below: (The following is Mr. Zhang's talk) There were 22 proposals in this conference, which can be summarized into three points: (1) Locust control regulations; (2) Locust collection technology; (3) Locust control funds. Regarding the regulations, the conference has revised and passed them separately and sent them to the Ministry of Industry for reference. Regarding the technology, it can be divided into two types: (1) those that can be promoted now; (2) those that still need to be researched. Regarding the funding, there were many proposals. The conference decided that the more important one was to ask the Ministry of Industry to transfer to the Executive Yuan to send a letter to the National Economic Commission or order the Ministry of Finance to raise funds specifically for the central and provincial locust control funds to solve the Chinese locust problem. The three items of regulations, technology, and funding must be planned and taken care of at the same time. In China's situation, the government should pay attention to a once-and-for-all solution. The so-called once-and-for-all solution is to reclaim all the wasteland where locusts occur. It is best to plant wheat, barley, and sorghum. Otherwise, it should be developed into forests, so that it must not be left barren. For example, in the Rocky Mountains of the United States, locusts and grasshoppers were a huge disaster decades ago, but after this method, they disappeared by themselves. If we wait until after the outbreak before driving them away, it is a bad policy. There are many new methods for locust control now, which can be divided into chemical, physical, and biological categories. Which method should China use after all? It should be adapted to local conditions to be effective. Later, the reporter asked about his impressions of the conference. According to him, recently, the government has been earnestly seeking to relieve the suffering of farmers and the prosperity of the national economy, such as the improvement of silk and tea, etc., which is enough to show a glimpse. Therefore, this trip was very impressive.

The Yang An Steamer of Sanbei Collided with a Civilian Boat in the Upper Reaches of the Yangtze River – Involved in a Lawsuit – A Towing Bamboo Raft Was Sunk – Both Crews Were Sent to Court for Interrogation 150

The Yang An steamer of the Sanbei Company was towing a barge to transport goods to Hunan. On the way, it collided with a civilian boat, drowning the boatman. The personnel on the steamer were involved in a lawsuit with the boatman's family in the Wuchang court. The details are as follows:

Ship Collision at Parrot Island 151

The Sanbei Yang An steamer, which operates on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, was towing the 13th and 17th iron barges, fully loaded with passengers and cargo, to Changsha for unloading on the 7th of this month. When the ship reached the Parrot Island section of the river upstream of Hankou, a civilian boat towing a large number of bamboo rafts was coming downstream. They encountered each other in the Parrot Island section of the river. Due to the rapid downstream current, the two ships collided when they approached each other. The stern of the civilian boat avoided the collision relatively late and was hit by the Yang An steamer, damaging the stern of the boat, but it did not sink.

Negotiations with the Civilian Boat 152

At the beginning of the incident, the circumstances were very minor. If the civilian boat had negotiated peacefully, an accident could have been avoided. Unexpectedly, after the civilian boat was hit, it gathered its fellow boatmen and seriously negotiated with the Yang An steamer. The Yang An steamer did not stop at that time and continued to move forward as usual. When the civilian boat chased after it and prohibited the Yang An from sailing upstream, demanding compensation for the loss, the river water was extremely turbulent. The Yang An steamer was towing a heavy barge, so it ordered the civilian boat to give way so that it could stop and negotiate. Unexpectedly, the civilian boat ignored it and blocked the river surface, causing a second collision when the Yang An stopped. The civilian boat sank immediately, and all the boatmen fell into the river.

One Person Drowned 153

The Yang An steamer's collision with the civilian boat was due to the civilian boat's failure to heed warnings. In the face of rising tides and rapid currents, it was its own fault. After stopping, it immediately rescued the people who fell into the water. The nearby civilian boats also came to help salvage. Many people were rescued on the spot. According to the owner of the civilian boat, one of the boatmen was said to have not been rescued and had drowned. The body was later salvaged, but it was not found. At this time, the owner of the civilian boat began to negotiate with the Yang An steamer, gathering a large number of barge operators and ordering the Yang An steamer to compensate for all the losses, which led to a major dispute.

Water Police Detain Crew Members 154

The Yang An steamer was trapped by the boatmen of the wrecked civilian boat and could not leave. The dispute continued in the Parrot Island section of the river. The local water police bureau learned about it and sent a group of police officers on a boat to investigate the cause. After inquiring about the case, it was found that each side had its own reasons and it was impossible to judge for the time being. The two boatmen of the Yang An steamer were detained by the water police, along with the owner of the damaged civilian boat, and taken back to Wuchang and sent to the court. The Yang An steamer continued to tow the heavily loaded iron barge upstream to Changsha. The two parties are still detained in the Wuchang court awaiting trial. The Hankou branch has urgently reported to the Shanghai head office and requested instructions.

Zhang Zhuying – Appeals the Zhou E'xuan Case – The Original Verdict is Revoked and Zhou is Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment 155

Zhou E'xuan, the eldest son of Zhou Weishi, the owner of the Zhou Gengji Yarn Shop, a wealthy merchant in Shanghai, was accused of abandoning his biological son, Zhou Dayuan, and failing to provide for his food and clothing. Dayuan's mother, Zhang Zhuying, hired a lawyer to sue E'xuan in the First Special District Court, asking him to be punished for the crime of abandonment. After being summoned by Judge Wu Zehan, Zhou E'xuan was found not guilty. The plaintiff was unwilling to accept the verdict and appealed to the Second Branch Court, requesting a retrial. Yu Hua, the presiding judge of the criminal court in charge of the case, again ordered Zhou, Zhang, and Dayuan to be re-examined by the Zhenru Forensic Institute. Subsequently, Lin Qi, the director of the institute, reported that the blood types of the three people were the same, and Dayuan's appearance was particularly similar to Zhou E'xuan, confirming that they were born to Zhou and Zhang. Last Tuesday, Judge Yu specially convened a collegial panel, summoning a thousand witnesses to investigate. All the witnesses who appeared in court, except Zhou's driver, said that the child was indeed born to Zhou and Zhang while they were living together at No. 8 Xinglongfang, Danshui Road. On that day, the court ordered the debate to end. Yesterday afternoon was the date of the verdict. Zhou E'xuan avoided appearing in court. At 2 p.m., the judge took the stand, and only Zhang Zhuying was present. After the court inquired about her name, age, and origin, the verdict was announced: "The part of the original verdict concerning Zhou E'xuan's innocence is revoked. Zhou E'xuan is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for failing to provide the necessary support for a person without the ability to support himself."

Gunmen Attack in Guangxi Road – Injured Policeman Dies – Court Investigation Held Yesterday 156

Chen Jing, an inspector of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was suddenly attacked by three gunmen on Guangxi Road at about 9 p.m. on the 9th of this month. At the same time, Chinese policeman No. 558 of the Laozha Gate Police Station, who was on duty at the intersection of Hankou Road, was also seriously injured in the leg. Both of them were injured and collapsed in pools of blood. The perpetrators took the opportunity to escape without a trace. After the Laozha Gate Police Station received the report and dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate, Chen and the Chinese policeman were sent to the hospital for treatment. It has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Chinese policeman's name was Wang Jinrong, 33 years old, from Shandong. He lived at No. 49 Xinzha Road. He had a wife and children at home, who depended on him for a living. Now, he was suddenly attacked by gunmen while on duty. Unexpectedly, his injury suddenly worsened the day before yesterday. He was treated in vain at the Municipal Council Hospital and died at about 10 p.m. The body was taken to the Forensic Institute on Faelun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Diao Chengtang, forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zujiong, and others to the institute to investigate the body. After the Western police chief reported the situation at the time, Mr. Diao then announced that the deceased, Wang Jinrong, had indeed been shot in the leg and died. The body was handed over to his wife, Wang Zhu, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial. It is now reported that the police are strictly pursuing the perpetrators.

Snake-Catching Old Beggar – Bitten by a Poisonous Snake – Fainted on the Spot and Became Unconscious – Later Woke Up Blind 157

There is an old beggar in Wusong, whose name is unknown. People call him Big Foot. He is nearly sixty years old. Although he is a beggar, he does not beg from door to door. He specializes in catching poisonous snakes, stripping their gallbladders, and selling them to those who suffer from eye diseases for treatment. Secondly, whenever there is a funeral procession, he acts as a guide and collects road money. Therefore, all the people in Song know Big Foot. As for his surgery of stripping snake gallbladders, it can be called the best. A few days ago, I saw him stripping a snake gallbladder without using knives or scissors, and it was not troublesome. He just stepped on the head and tail of the snake with his two feet, opened it with his two fingers on the abdomen, tore it down, and immediately took out the bloody, green snake gallbladder from the intestines, immediately in his palm. However, the poisonous snake at that time was still alive as before, without any pain of having been taken away from its heart and gallbladder. Later, he used a broken brick to flatten the snake's head before it died. Yesterday, Big Foot went to the countryside to catch snakes again and found a small poisonous snake about a foot long. Because he saw that the snake was small, he did not pretend and grabbed it with his hand. Unexpectedly, the little snake bit his ring finger severely, and the skin on his hand was slightly broken. However, the poison was deep and painful to the heart. Knowing that it was not good, he rushed back to his residence. Although he rushed back, he was exhausted and hoarse, and immediately fell to the ground, unconscious. Later, he was rescued and woke up, but he was blind in both eyes, and his fingers were swollen all the way to his shoulders, as big as a human leg. The speed of the spread of the poison was alarming. Although he knew the treatment method, because he was so severely poisoned, his life was in danger. Knowing that he could not do anything, he immediately ordered someone to go to Shanghai to find someone with the same business in Ningbo (whose poison treatment method is better than Big Foot) to come to Song for treatment. The poison has now subsided slightly, and his life may be saved. According to him, it is because he usually kills too many snakes that he is now receiving retribution. However, now is the Dragon Boat Festival, when all kinds of poisons are released. Those who carry burdens on their shoulders and walk at night should pay close attention to avoid stepping on poisonous objects, which may cause danger.

French Concession Pawnshop Street – Busts Red Pill Factory – Manufacturing Secretly at Midnight to Avoid Suspicion – The Main Culprit is at Large and Four People are Arrested 158

Wang Rusong, a detective of the French Police Department, Zhang Daorong, a deputy detective, and detectives Wang Dongwan and Guo Shaotang, recently learned that someone was secretly setting up a mechanism to manufacture poisonous red pills in a house at No. 3 Huashengfang, Diandang Street, outside the Old North Gate. To avoid suspicion, they started manufacturing every night when it was quiet and stopped working at dawn. The goods produced were sold as No. 11 (goods name) in this city and the surrounding areas, making a lot of profit. They immediately reported to the Western Police Chief, who went to the address at 4:30 a.m. yesterday without making a sound and searched the premises. The manufacturing mechanism was set up in the pavilion room upstairs. The workers were manufacturing when they were arrested on the spot: Zhou Fuqing (23 years old, from Yangzhou), Ding Wancai (23 years old, from Yangzhou), Chen Chunyin (26 years old, from Jiangbei), Yuan Hongcai (20 years old, from Chongming), and other four people. Forty pounds of finished red pills, fifty pounds of unfinished ingredients, a pill-making board, three ovens, four sieves, a copying pill board, a small bag of coffee sugar, two scales, two cups of fire paint, two bundles of hemp rope, and two large foot basins were seized. It was learned that the leader of the mechanism lived elsewhere. Zhou and other four criminals, along with the evidence, were taken to the police station and sent to the Criminal Court 1 of the Second Special District Court at noon on the same day. Judge Xiong Huiyi took the stand for interrogation. Fei Xizhen, the lawyer representing the police department, stated the case and said that the main culprit in the case had not been caught, and the investigation had not yet begun. He requested a postponement and temporarily detained the defendants to investigate the detailed facts of the case and file a lawsuit, etc., and submitted the evidence to the court. After reviewing the report, the court ordered the police officer in charge to report the details of the arrest and briefly interrogated the defendants. The court then approved the postponement and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody to await further instructions.

Former Qing Daotai Chen Hansen's Home

One Hundred Thousand Yuan of Government Bonds Stolen – =Chen Afu, a Former Chauffeur, is the Most Suspected= – =Arrested and Detained for Two Days for Further Interrogation= 160

Chen Hansen, a Fujianese who once served as a Daotai in the late Qing Dynasty, built a Western-style residence at No. 4 Mandelan Road. He employed seven male and female servants in his home. In April of last year, he hired Chen Afu, a Yangzhou native, as a chauffeur, who was guaranteed by Ma Lishi's employment agency. He has been serving for more than a year. On the 26th of last month, Chen entertained guests at home. Chen Afu wanted to go out for entertainment but was stopped by his master, which caused a slight dispute, and Afu was dismissed. On the 9th of this month, Chen Hansen suddenly discovered that 100,590 yuan of military reduction government bonds, which were stored in his iron box, including 100 bonds worth 1,000 yuan each and 590 bonds worth 10 yuan each, had disappeared. Afu's guarantee, which had been submitted earlier, was also missing at the same time. It was found that Chen had invested in buying the government bonds in 1929, and the bonds were stored in the iron box in the upstairs bedroom, along with Afu's guarantee. There were two keys in total, one held by Chen and the other by his wife. A few days ago, Chen's wife returned to Shanghai from her hometown and wanted to withdraw interest from the bank, so she opened the box to check and discovered that the bonds had been stolen. He reported the theft to the Chengdu Road Police Station and asked for an investigation, saying that Afu had gone to his home to ask for the guarantee after being dismissed, and was highly suspected. The police chief sent Chinese detectives Yang Xinzheng and Bao Tingwei to arrest Chen Afu yesterday morning and take him to the police station for detention. This morning, he was sent to the Criminal Court 2 of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Zhang Shizhu rose and stated the course of events, saying that the police still needed to investigate whether Chen Afu was suspected of stealing the government bonds. Therefore, he requested that Chen be detained for two days for further interrogation. After Chen Susou, Chen Hansen's son, complained about the theft, Chen Afu was questioned and denied the theft. After reviewing the confession, Judge Deng Baosun announced that Chen could be detained for two days for further interrogation.

Electric Torch Explodes – Death and Injury Lawsuit – Confirmed Injury Resulting in Death – Judge Orders Transfer to Local Court for Trial 161

The Gongji Zhongyu Electric Pole Iron Factory, located at the intersection of Huade Road and Baoding Road, was opened by Wang Jinsheng. Li Cungui and Li Cunfang, both from Anhui, were casual workers in the factory. At noon on the 28th of last month, the two Lis were sent to work in the iron-sheet house at No. 594 Kunming Road, plating electric poles on iron tubes. Unexpectedly, due to a moment of carelessness, the electric tube suddenly exploded, causing Li Cungui to die on the spot. Li Cunfang's left leg was blown off. At that time, Cungui's wife, Li Cai, also known as Genmei, who was only sixteen years old, and Cunfang's younger brother, Li Mohai, who was thirteen years old, were also injured when they went to the place to ask the two Lis to go home for lunch. Mohai was injured in the face, and Cai was injured in the left leg. Afterwards, the injured were sent to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment, and the deceased Li Cungui was sent to the coroner's office. The court has investigated the details. It has been reported in this newspaper. However, after the incident, the families of the dead and injured went to the Zhongxing Electric Pole Factory to negotiate, but the factory owner Wang Jinsheng avoided meeting them and secretly instigated the local hooligan Xiao Wang to come forward to threaten them, intending to muddle through. However, because it was rumored that the factory owner had given Xiao Wang 1,000 yuan, he was not allowed. Li Cunfang, Li Li (Cunfang's wife), Li Mohai, Li Cai, and others hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Wang Jinsheng of the crime of negligent injury under Article 301 of the Criminal Law, and Xiao Wang of the crime of fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Law, requesting that the two defendants be summoned to court for interrogation according to law, and attached a civil lawsuit, requesting compensation of 3,000 yuan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng presided over the hearing in Criminal Court 5. The plaintiffs appeared in court one after another and stated the course of events. The defendant hired lawyer Huang Xiubo to defend him. Judge Huang ruled that the case involved the crime of injury resulting in death under Article 296 of the Criminal Law, which was a local case, and ordered that the case be transferred to the local court for trial.

Communication from the Tongru Chonghai Qi Hometown Association: A Plea Regarding Cai Yangqi's Ordeal of Electric Torture 163

The Tongru Chonghai Qi Five-County Sojourners' Association in Shanghai, yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Citizens' Federation and major organizations in this port, which read: "Respected Sirs, our fellow townsman, Cai Yangqi, an investigator for the Old Zhabei Police Station, was subjected to cruel and unusual punishment by Lang Zuyin. This case has been reported repeatedly and has been protested by the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. We have learned that Cai Yangqi has lived in Qiyao, Chongming, for generations and is an extremely honest and reliable person. He has been working in the local goods industry in Shanghai for ten years and has never been involved in any illegal activities. Since this case occurred, our association has sent people to investigate and is convinced that he was innocently framed. He was subjected to electric torture seventeen times by police station detectives and had cold water poured into his nose, repeatedly dying and reviving. After the court declared him innocent and released him, he vomited blood uncontrollably and was on the verge of death. He has reached a state where he cannot recover his health. Hearing him recount the details of his torture, even those with hearts of stone could not help but shed tears. This kind of inhumane crime actually occurred in a police station that claims to be civilized, which is truly astonishing. It has come to our attention that Shanghai's investigators (omission) and the Municipal Council has taken no corrective action. Do they regard Shanghai as a savage place, and therefore use this cruel and inhumane illegal behavior as a legitimate way to maintain order and tranquility? If this kind of situation occurred in countries like England and America, how would it be handled? We believe that the police station authorities are supported by the taxpayers and are fully responsible for local security. Achieving the best results by effectively reducing crime is the highest achievement. If, after a crime occurs, the perpetrators are apprehended by legitimate means, it is also welcomed by society. If cruel punishment is occasionally inflicted on extremely violent thieves and kidnappers who are not afraid of the law, although it is not permitted by law, it may be understood by the people as a necessity. However, to subject anyone to severe and cruel torture based solely on the arbitrary actions of investigators, without investigating their usual conduct or considering the evidence, except for those with special influence or a large amount of money, is unacceptable. Under such duress, anything can be obtained. Those who have been wronged have no way to appeal. Only a very small number of cases like Cai Yangqi's are made public. Where is the protection of human rights? Where is the effectiveness of the law? All Shanghai residents are deeply saddened and indignant. Therefore, they regard the Cai Yangqi case as a serious social problem. The police station's use of electric torture is an open secret, and the protection of investigators is dedicated to unconscionable deeds, which is even more offensive to the people. If this is not strictly corrected, how can any resident of Shanghai protect themselves? Since the Chinese Ratepayers' Association protested, the Municipal Council has not taken appropriate measures, and the police station has instead protected investigator Lang Zuyin, who refuses to appear in court. Justice has been extinguished, and indignation is boundless. Our association has repeatedly convened meetings and believes that punishing the investigators who committed the crime is a matter for the court, but preventing similar cases from happening again is the responsibility of society. Your federation is the representative of the people of Shanghai and must work together to protest and urge the Chinese directors and committee members to do their best to assist in upholding justice and human rights. We are extremely grateful and await your instructions." Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Citizens' Federation, Tongru Chonghai Qi Five-County Sojourners' Association. (Guowen News Agency)
